The Derailment of a Freight Train on the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway Was Fully Repaired Yesterday Morning 121

The 321st down-train freight train on the Nanjing-Shanghai Railway derailed at Benniu Station at 9:00 AM the day before yesterday, causing the locomotive and four freight cars to overturn. The railway's traffic and engineering departments successively dispatched rescue trains from Shanghai and Changzhou to rush to repair the damage. At 7:00 PM that evening, temporary tracks were first laid to facilitate traffic. At the same time, the derailed freight cars were lifted and the track timbers were repaired. The work was completed at around 6:00 AM yesterday morning, restoring the original condition.

Fully Repaired Because the derailed freight cars on the Nanjing-Shanghai Railway were fully loaded with goods and difficult to lift, temporary tracks were rushed to completion at 7:06 PM that evening, allowing all trains to pass without obstruction. At the same time, coolies were ordered to unload the goods from each car before lifting the cars and dragging them away from the scene of the accident. The sleepers and steel rails were rushed to repair, and the entire project was completed at around 6:00 AM yesterday morning, restoring the original condition. All trains arrived at their destinations on time.

Consulting on Aftermath The Traffic Department and Engineering Department of the railway dispatched responsible persons and engineers to the scene of the accident for investigation and rescue after the accident. Although the tracks have been repaired, in order to investigate the cause of the accident and its responsibility, a meeting was held at Benniu Station at 9:00 AM yesterday morning. Those present included Yuan Shaochang, Deputy Director of the Traffic Department; Chen Chengshi, Chief of the Nanjing-Shanghai Main Section; Xu Chaoyuan, Deputy Section Chief; Lü Weiyan, Chief of the Dan-Su Sub-Section; Tang Huanfu, Chief of the Resident Section; Huai Haoshide, Director of the Engineering Department; Zhong En, Deputy Director of the Locomotive Department; Feng Qili, Chief Engineer of Shanghai Station; and the stationmaster at the scene of the accident and his responsible personnel.

The Dada Company's Jiangjing Steamer Returned to Shanghai Yesterday 123

Passengers Secretly Carried Explosives That Evaporated and Exploded

On the 3rd of this month, it departed from Shanghai to Tongyang. When it arrived above Xinsheng Port, passengers on board secretly carried explosives and sulfur, which suddenly exploded. Two crew members and five passengers were wounded on the spot, and part of the ship's cabin was also damaged. The passengers who caused the accident have been detained and sent to the Jiangyin Public Security Bureau for interrogation. The Jiangjing returned to Shanghai yesterday. The situation investigated by this newspaper's reporter is recorded below:

The Equipment Inside the Ship Is Complete Since the Great Auspicious disaster two years ago, in which the Dagil was loaded with saltpeter, causing a huge explosion, the Dada Shipping Company's Tongyang-bound ships have been very thorough in their arrangement of fire-fighting equipment inside the ship. They do not load dangerous goods or explosives. Also, fearing that passengers may secretly transport prohibited items, and for the safety of the voyage, the company has also consulted with the water police to accompany the ship and inspect along the way. All matters related to eliminating crises are actively carried out, and the fire prevention and inspection of the Jiangjing is even more strictly enforced. Unexpectedly, there was still an explosion caused by secretly carried explosives and saltpeter.

Passengers Secretly Carried Explosives The Jiangjing Steamer departed from Shanghai at around 2:00 PM on the 3rd of this month. There were not many goods leaving Shanghai, but there were more than 400 passengers, and more luggage than usual. When the ship left Shanghai, several passengers, including Cai Yunsheng, Zou Caigao, and Zhang Yucun, each carried objects in mesh baskets. When boarding the ship, they were received by the tea boy and stayed in the cabin on the platform deck in the front cargo hold. Initially, it was not expected that the mesh baskets secretly carried dangerous goods such as explosives and saltpeter.

Sudden Explosion En Route At around 6:00 PM, when the ship arrived in the middle of Xinsheng Port and Xin Port, the ship served dinner and prepared for bed. The explosives and saltpeter in the mesh baskets on the upper layer of the front cargo hold suddenly exploded due to heat evaporation. With a loud bang, the entire ship shook. After the explosion, flames immediately rose, and the smell of saltpeter filled the entire ship. All cabins were shrouded in smoke.

Passengers Panicked Suddenly hearing the smell of smoke, the passengers suspected that the boiler in the engine room had exploded, believing that a great disaster was about to happen. More than 400 passengers rushed out of the cabin, scurrying towards the bow and stern of the ship, hoping to escape. The order was disrupted as a result. Some passengers, seeing smoke rising from the head cabin, jumped into the river and swam away. The ship was on the verge of capsizing due to the passengers running to one side. Fortunately, the shipowner and crew made every effort to explain and persuade, so the situation was turned around.

The Truth of the Cause of the Accident Was Ascertained While the shipowner was appeasing the passengers, he ordered all the crew and sailors to use the fire-fighting equipment on board and make every effort to extinguish the smoke and fire in the head cabin. After an hour, the remaining fire was extinguished. Someone was sent to thoroughly investigate the truth of the accident. The watchman, Chen Fusheng, witnessed the explosion in the cabin on the second floor of the head cabin. Cai Yunsheng, Zou Caigao, Zhang Yucun, and others were carrying mesh baskets. The watchman pointed out that the three were the ones who secretly carried explosives. Another passenger named Liu Guangcheng also secretly carried saltpeter. The crew put the four of them under guard. A Total of Seven People Were Injured

The explosion occurred in the rear section of the second floor of the head cabin. Those injured in the explosion were: Liu Guangcheng, 38 years old, from Funing, injured in the face, residing at Shunde Lane, Hartung Road, Shanghai, a pastor at the Jesus Church; (2) Li Amei, 14 years old, from Yangzhou, injured in the head and left hand and foot, almost severed, working in a yarn factory in Shanghai; (3) Zhou Changluo, 29 years old, from Yangzhou, injured in the face, a deckhand on the ship; (4) Liu Yinchun, from Xin Port, injured in both feet; (5) Wang Yungen, 32 years old, from Yangzhou, a shoemaker, injured in the face; (6) Qian Bingheng, from Zhenjiang, 40 years old, a freight accountant on the Jiangjing, injured in the face; (7) Shen Huanzuo, from Wuxi, 24 years old, a ticket inspector on the ship, injured in the face.

Sent to the Jiangyin Hospital and Bureau After the accident, the ship immediately sailed to Jiangyin and reported to the Public Security Bureau. Director Hua sent patrol officer Wu Guoan to thoroughly investigate the ship. The perpetrators, Cai Yunsheng (from Wuling), Zou Caigao (from Yancheng),

Zhang Yucun, Liu Guangcheng, and others were taken to the bureau. A business card and certificate from Wang Zemin, a saltpeter salesman in the Shangbao District, were found on each person. The Public Security Bureau, considering that the matter concerned the secret carrying of prohibited items and caused a major disaster, immediately transferred them to the Jiangyin County Government for interrogation. As for the seven injured people, they were also transferred to the Northeast Gate Gospel Hospital for treatment. It is said that Li Amei was the most seriously injured, with his limbs severed. The other three who were injured in the face were blinded in both eyes and could not be treated, and will be disabled. The Shipowner's Original Telegram The shipowner sent a telegram to Shanghai to report to the Dada Company, Jiangjing was between Xinsheng Port and Xin Port at youke evening. In the front cargo hold, there was a sudden explosion, the smell of sulfur, the fire and smoke were everywhere, and the order was in chaos. The ship was almost overturned. Fortunately, it was rescued immediately and extinguished immediately. The fire chief Qian and the inspector Shen were injured, as well as four others, and sent to Jiangyin Hospital. The perpetrator of the explosives was sent to the Public Security Bureau and interrogated by the county. There was slight damage to the goods. When the telegram arrived, it was a Sunday, and no one was working, so it was not forwarded to the China Merchants Bureau until yesterday morning, and the bureau forwarded it to the insurance company for reference.

Slight Damage to the Ship's Hull Returned to Shanghai, The ship has returned to Shanghai via Yangzhou and Tongzhou, arriving at the port at 3:00 PM and docking at the Dada Wharf in Nanshi. The explosion destroyed six passenger seats on the second floor of the front cabin, and the ship's hull was slightly damaged. All the explosive mesh baskets were destroyed, but the empty shells of the firecrackers were brought to Shanghai by the shipowner for the company to view. The damage to the front cabin was reported to the China Merchants Bureau, which sent carpenters and workers to repair it. The ship will operate as usual today.

Shanghai-Hankou Through Train Service Commenced Yesterday 124

First Train from Hankou Will Arrive in Shanghai on the Evening of the 7th

Train from Shanghai Will Arrive in Hankou on the Morning of the 8th

The Shanghai-Hankou through train service commenced yesterday, with one train running daily in each direction between Shanghai and Hankou. The Shanghai-Xuzhou section will temporarily use the Shanghai-Beijing through train. The journey will take approximately 50 hours. First, second, and third-class sleeper tickets are available. The details are as follows:

Commencement of Through Train Service The Shanghai-Hankou through train service was implemented yesterday after the Nanjing-Shanghai, Tianjin-Pukou, Longhai, and Beijing-Hankou railways completed their preparations. Train No. 302, the Shanghai-Beijing through train, departs from Shanghai North Station at 12:00 PM. Passenger Train No. 2 departs from Dazhimen, Hankou, at 10:30 PM. The Shanghai-Xuzhou section of the train from Shanghai to Hankou temporarily uses the Shanghai-Beijing through train. After arriving in Xuzhou, the Longhai Railway will have one first/second-class passenger/sleeper mixed car and one third-class car attached to Passenger Train No. 1 to Zhengzhou, and then transfer to Hankou. The train from Hankou to Shanghai will have Passenger Train No. 2 attached to the Beijing-Hankou Railway to Zhengzhou, then Passenger Train No. 2 attached to the Longhai Railway to Xuzhou, and then transfer to Train No. 301, the Shanghai-Beijing through train, on the Tianjin-Pukou Railway to Shanghai.

Train Schedule The train schedule for the Shanghai-Hankou through train is as follows: (1) From Hankou to Shanghai on the Beijing-Hankou Railway, departing from Dazhimen, Hankou, at 10:30 PM, arriving in Zhengzhou at 4:30 PM the next day. The Longhai Railway departs from Zhengzhou at 7:00 PM, arriving in Xuzhou at 5:15 AM the next day. The Tianjin-Pukou Railway departs from Xuzhou at 6:20 AM, arriving at Shanghai North Station on the Nanjing-Shanghai Railway at 11:05 PM that afternoon. (2) From Shanghai to Hankou, the Nanjing-Shanghai Railway departs from Shanghai North Station at 12:00 PM, arriving in Xuzhou on the Tianjin-Pukou Railway at 8:12 PM the next day. The Longhai Railway departs from Xuzhou at 9:10 PM, arriving in Zhengzhou at 8:49 AM the next day. It was originally planned to connect with Train No. 1 on the Beijing-Hankou Railway, but the Beijing-Hankou Railway departs from Zhengzhou at 7:11 PM. Now, considering that the time difference is too long, the Ministry of Railways has decided to dispatch a special train from the Beijing-Hankou Railway to pick up the train arriving in Zhengzhou at 8:49 AM.

Arrival Dates The total travel time from Hankou to Shanghai is 49 hours and 25 minutes. The first through train from Hankou yesterday is scheduled to arrive at Shanghai North Station at 11:55 PM on the 7th. The through train from Shanghai to Hankou, the Beijing-Hankou Railway has designated a special train from Zhengzhou to Hankou, but the timings have not been fixed. The travel time is approximately 50 hours. The first through train departed from Shanghai North Station at 12:00 PM yesterday, and is expected to arrive at Dazhimen Station in Hankou on the morning of the 8th.

Iron Department Limits Payment Methods for Intermodal Transport of Goods 125

Should be limited to payment in advance or on arrival according to regulations

It is not permissible for each railway to collect separately, hindering progress. The Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administration received instructions from the Ministry of Railways stating: "According to the intermodal transport report, the original principle for payment methods for responsible intermodal transport of goods by railways was limited to two types: payment in advance or payment on arrival. However, the intermodal transport handled by the Pinghan and Longhai Railways, as well as the Jinpu and Jiaoji Railways, sometimes uses a payment method of one ticket with two types of payment (i.e., payment in advance at the departure station and payment on arrival at the destination station), which is not convenient for merchants and hinders the promotion of intermodal transport. It is proposed to order the cancellation of this method."

Upon investigation, the payment method for intermodal transport of goods, as stipulated in the "Provisional Measures for Responsible Intermodal Transport of Goods by Railways" promulgated by the Ministry, was originally limited to payment in advance or payment on arrival. If these railways continue to follow old practices and each railway collects its own fees, it may appear to be intermodal transport on the surface, but in reality, it is simply the transfer of vehicles from one track to another. This not only contradicts the intermodal transport regulations but also greatly hinders the promotion of intermodal transport. Since the restoration of responsible intermodal transport of goods by railways, this payment method has no room for existence. If all railways involved in intermodal transport only focus on absorbing current cash flow, disregarding the regulations promulgated by the Ministry and the interests of merchants, the result will inevitably affect the national intermodal transport industry.

To prevent problems before they arise, it is hereby ordered that all relevant railways comply with the following: henceforth, for all payment methods at each station for intermodal transport, payment shall uniformly be limited to payment in advance or on arrival according to regulations. It is not permissible to adhere to old practices and have each railway collect its own fees, which would hinder the convenience of merchants and the promotion of intermodal transport. In addition to separately ordering all intermodal transport railway bureaus to comply, you are hereby ordered to strictly comply with and implement this order." The bureau has already instructed the transportation department to comply.

In the Midst of Calls for Relief for Native Sugar, Qinzhou-Lianzhou Native Sugar is Confiscated Again 126

Pang Songhui petitions in Beijing again. Pang Songhui, a representative of sugar merchants from Qinzhou and Lianzhou, was entrusted by the chambers of commerce of various counties in Qinzhou and Lianzhou and the Guangyi Hall of the sugar industry to petition in Beijing because the Jianghai Customs repeatedly detained and fined native sugar from Qinzhou and Lianzhou being transported to Shanghai last year. This matter has been reported in various newspapers. Representative Pang previously arrived in Shanghai and appealed for assistance from the National Federation of Commerce, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, and other organizations. He also petitioned the Executive Yuan, the Ministry of Finance, the Ministry of Industry, and the Customs Administration in Beijing, presenting four relief measures, which were all adopted. Sugar farmers and merchants who had been forced out of work for several months resumed their businesses this year because the government promised to protect them. However, the Jianghai Customs' sugar inspection has not only failed to correct its errors but has actually intensified them.

On the 23rd of last month, Henghelong, a Qinzhou-Lianzhou sugar merchant, transported 92 packages of native white sugar from Beihai to Shanghai on the Hubei steamer, which was received by Futian Foreign Firm. When exporting, the Beihai Customs verified that the sugar was produced by the Lunchang Sugar Workshop in Wuli Market, Lingshan County, and was indeed a pure native product. Upon arrival in Shanghai, the Jianghai Customs re-examined it and unexpectedly claimed that it contained more than half foreign sugar and confiscated the entire shipment.

Representative Pang returned to Shanghai from Beijing upon hearing the news and rushed to the Jianghai Customs to question the Deputy Commissioner of Customs. It was claimed that the sugar had a specific rotation of 92.8 degrees, which proved that it contained more than half foreign sugar. Representative Pang argued that the Central Industrial Testing Laboratory was ordered last month to test native sugar from Qiongzhou, and type C had a specific rotation of 92 degrees, while type B reached 93 degrees. Native sugar from Qinzhou and Lianzhou has always been better than that from Qiongzhou. Now that the sugar has been tested and has not reached 93 degrees, how can it be said that it contains foreign sugar? He requested that it be retained for public re-examination.

Subsequently, Representative Pang, accompanied by Zheng Zenan, chairman of the Sugar Industry Association, went to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to report the matter. Chairman Wang Xiaolai, Secretary Yan E, and others were shocked upon hearing the news. They all believed that the Jianghai Customs' actions would not stop until native sugar was completely destroyed and unanimously agreed to forward the matter to the central government for urgent relief measures. It is reported that Representative Pang will again go to the Jianghai Customs Supervisory Office, the National Tariff Commission, the National Federation of Commerce, the Guangdong Fellow Association, and other organizations to appeal for relief and assistance, and then petition in Beijing again.

Bureau of International Trade Announces Reasons for Failure of Chinese Goods Sales in New Zealand 127

Silk and tea urgently need improvement. Yesterday, He Bingxian, Director of the Bureau of International Trade, and Ji Zejin, Director of the Guidance Department, discussed the trade situation between China and New Zealand and the reasons for its failure. The main Chinese goods sold in New Zealand are hardware, dried fruit, silk, cloth, and the like. The value of goods imported last year (1932) was 82,115 New Zealand pounds, a decrease of more than 2,600 pounds compared to the import volume in 1931 and a decrease of more than 54,500 pounds compared to the import volume in 1928.

The biggest reason for this is the global economic recession. In the past two or three years, unemployment in New Zealand has been very high, and purchasing power has been greatly weakened. Goods from all countries shipped to New Zealand have been affected. However, some Chinese goods have lost market share due to competition. Taking tea and silk as examples, they were originally unique products of China, and China originally monopolized the New Zealand market. In recent years, due to competition from tea and silk from other countries, the import of Chinese tea and silk has decreased sharply and declined year by year. The tea and silk market that once belonged to us has been seized by Indian, Ceylonese tea, English and Japanese silk.

The reasons for the failure, taking tea as an example, are: first, the packaging is poor and traditional methods are adhered to. China and New Zealand are far apart, and there is a tropical zone in between. Most tea is still packaged in paper. By the time it arrives in New Zealand, the tea flavor has dissipated. Second, the credit of Chinese merchants is not stable. The samples sent do not match the goods, and the samples are often very good, while the goods are extremely poor, losing the trust of New Zealand merchants. Third, New Zealand imposes preferential tariffs on imports of British products, and Chinese tea is subject to higher taxes, resulting in slightly higher costs and higher prices, leading to its defeat by Indian and Ceylonese tea.

Taking silk as an example, the color dyeing of Chinese silk is not top-notch, and the material is strong and thick, but the price is too expensive, making it difficult to compete with cheap Japanese silk. Silk fabrics are used to make women's fashion, and the patterns and styles are changing with each passing day. Therefore, although Chinese silk is durable, it is not valued. Since 1928, the value of Chinese goods sold in New Zealand has gradually declined. The reason for this is the global economic recession. It is hoped that the import of Chinese goods will increase when the world becomes prosperous. However, if goods such as tea and silk have lost market share due to competition, if we do not improve our shortcomings, how can we compete with others and how can we restore the old rules?

Crackdown on Unlicensed Seafarers Extended to the End of June 128

All must apply for inspection according to law within the time limit. According to New Voice News Agency, since the Ministry of Transportation promulgated the "Provisional Regulations for Seafarer Inspection", it has held seafarer examinations twice and has cracked down on the continued employment of unlicensed seafarers who have not applied for inspection. It is also stipulated that all must apply for inspection according to law within this period. If they still wait and see, they will be subject to crackdown at that time. Jianghai Customs Issues Two Notices 129

New weights and measures must indicate the conversion number of old weights and measures.

Add items to the import manifest.

The General Affairs Department of the Jianghai Customs, in order to implement the new system of weights and measures, temporarily requires indicating the conversion number of the old system of weights and measures, and adding items to the import manifest, issued notices No. 28 and 29 yesterday as follows:

Notice 1: The new system of weights and measures is scheduled to be implemented on February 1 of this year. This Customs has already issued announcement No. 1328. Within three weeks from the date of implementation of the new system of weights and measures, the new system of weights and measures and the conversion number according to the old system of weights and measures must be indicated separately. All merchants, etc., are requested to comply. This is hereby announced.

Notice 2: The matter of submitting inspection forms for ships entering port according to the rules for a trial period was announced by this Customs on March 20 of the 20th year of the Republic of China. Hereafter, one of the following items must be filled in on all import manifests submitted to the Customs: (1) Packing list attached; (2) There is no package on board. All circumstances of the package carried should be listed in the packing list and must be signed by the shipowner of the ship taken for verification. All shipping merchants, etc., are requested to comply. This is hereby announced.

Ministry of Transportation Stipulates Routes for Transmitting Official Public Telegrams 130

Divide wireless stations into four routes.

Yesterday, the Municipal Radio Station was ordered to comply with the matter of transmitting official public telegrams. The Municipal Radio Station received an order from the Ministry of Transportation yesterday stating: "In order to comply with the matter, although there are special designated routes for transmitting official public telegrams to various stations, the sending station often has not been registered. By the time it reaches other places, the relay station adds the registration, so that one telegram is often received from several places and forwarded repeatedly, which not only consumes electricity and materials, but also clogs the circuit. The wireless stations under the Ministry are now divided into four routes for receiving and relaying such official public telegrams: Wuhu, Ningbo, Chongming, Nanjing, Dinghai, Xiamen, Fuzhou, Guangzhou, Shantou, Qidong, and other ten places are the first route; Nanchang, Yichang, Shashi, Changsha, Xi'an, Lanzhou, and other six places are the second route; Weihaiwei, Qingdao, Beiping, Zhengzhou, Luoyang, Dihua, Yantai, Jinan, and other eight places are the third route; Xuzhou, Wanxian, Chengdu, Guiyang, Yunnan, and other five places are the fourth route. Any radio station in any route that receives an official public telegram should, in addition to sending it to the designated Shanghai, Hankou, Tianjin, and Chongqing radio stations within the route, not forward it on its own. Those that cannot be directly sent should be handed over in succession for other stations to forward to the designated relay station. After receiving the telegram, they should send it according to the route to avoid omissions. This will be implemented from March 1. You are hereby ordered to comply."

Rent Increase Wave in Fansheng Lane, Zhaofeng Road, Hongkou 132

Tenants form rent reduction branch to cope. The houses in Fansheng Lane, at the intersection of Zhaofeng Road and Dongxi Huade Road in Hongkou, are the property of Han Ronggen and are leased by the British company, Teli & Co. On the 17th of last month, the company suddenly appointed lawyer Chen Zhongyin to notify each tenant in writing that the rent would be increased by 30% from January. If they do not pay the increased amount in full, they will be ordered to pay off the old rent owed by the end of this month and move out. The tenants believe that the rent in this lane was increased by 20% in 1925. The landlord is taking advantage of the current economic downturn and commercial decline to implement high pressure by relying on the power of foreigners, which is hateful. Caoxi District Security Corps Busts Fake Lead Coin Machine 135

Shen Yunpu, platoon leader of the Xiaozha sub-defense of the Caoxi District Security Corps in Shanghai West, led squad leader Zhou Fugen and others on patrol outside last night at about 11 o'clock, when they caught sight of two people carrying cloth bags and walking in a panic at the intersection of Zhongshan Road. They immediately went forward to carry out an inspection. When the two people saw this, they abandoned their bags and fled, but were intercepted by the team members. Four people from Haimen who manufactured lead coins, Wang Deshun, Zhou Shaolong, Lu Qiuyang, and Lu Qiuming, were arrested on the spot and sent to the regiment headquarters. Xu Jinqing Commits Suicide in Frustration After His Job Search Fails and He is Scammed 136

Xu Jinqing, 19 years old, from Chang'an, came to Shanghai with his wife on January 23 to look for a job, temporarily staying in Room 96 of the Southeast Hotel in Taiyuanfang No. 8, Eddoya Road. Two weeks ago, he asked a friend to recommend him for a job, but it has not been successful so far. More than 70 yuan of the 120 yuan he brought with him was scammed by his friend. Therefore, Jinqing was extremely depressed and suddenly had the idea of ​​ending his life. Suddenly, last night, he went to the Faxing Hotel on Baliqiao Road in the French Concession alone to open Room 11. At that time, he paid 50 cents for the room and went to bed after closing the door. At about 11 o'clock yesterday morning, the tea room saw that the guest in the room had not gotten up yet, so he was quite suspicious. He tried to pry open the door and saw Xu lying on his back on the bed with a pale face and groaning. He knew that he had taken poison, and there was still a little opium left on the table that had not been swallowed. He immediately reported to the accounting room and forwarded the report to the police. Police officer No. 114 was sent to investigate and the poisoned person was taken to Renji Hospital for treatment. However, because he was deeply poisoned, the treatment was ineffective. He died at about 2 pm and was transferred to the post-mortem examination for examination.

Two pistols and eighty bullets

The police officer immediately reported to District Chief Lai, and sent patrol officer Peng Wenwei, led by police chief Sun Kezhi, police officers Zhong Zhong, Li Deshan, Yu Changle, etc., to the address. Together with the detective team in charge, they went to the attic of No. 9 Zudeli and arrested Zhu Jinzhang, seizing two six-inch Browning pistols, numbers 404347 and 404220, as well as eighty bullets and three magazines. Twenty pawn tickets were also seized. Five suspects, Zhou Chengzhi, Liu Naigong, Li Shixun, Jia Guixuan, and Cui Ruizhi, were also arrested downstairs. After being brought back, Zhu Jinzhang confessed that he was 28 years old and from Yancheng. He had not robbed in the Chinese Concession. The robbers Wang Songting, Tang Laoshi Zi, Xiao Sanzi, and Jin Da had robbed the Bin Cheng Yarn Factory in the Concession, obtaining 1,740 yuan in silver and two pistols. Fang Zhongshu bought them on behalf of Qin Yuqing and sent them to me. Wang Songting and others have disappeared, but Qin Yuqing lives on a boat at Dayang Bridge, but I don't know where she is now. Fang Zhongshu lives at No. 7, Zhudetongli, Binlang Road. Zhou Chengqia and the other five people are all living together and have nothing to do with it.

Subsequently, Zhou Chengzhi, 35 years old, from Anhui, Liu Naigong, 22 years old, Yu Tongqing, Li Shixun, 36 years old, Jia Guixuan, 24 years old (both from Hebei), and Cui Ruizhi, 36 years old, all confessed that they were living together and did not admit that they were companions with Zhu Jinzhang. After reviewing the confession, the interrogator ordered that Wang Songting, Tang Laoshi Zi, Xiao Sanzi, and Jin Da be arrested in addition to the case, and that the six criminals, Zhu Jinzhang, the suspected criminals, Zhu Songting, etc., along with two pistols, eighty bullets, and twenty pawn tickets, be escorted to the Public Security Bureau for disposal.

Extortion Case to be Pronounced 138

Chen Hesong, a native of Ningbo, 39 years old, who runs the Maolin Hardware and Sail Shop at No. 1002 Dongbai Laohui Road, returned to Ningbo by boat on January 27 due to some matters. First, at 3 pm, he took his own car to the home of his father-in-law, Xin Zihuai (mistakenly reported as his friend Shen Zihuai), at No. 8 Ningfuli, Gelock Road, French Concession, to say goodbye. Xin happened to be out. Chen was talking with his mother-in-law, Xin Jiangshi, for about three minutes when Hu Quanhai, a fellow villager he knew who lived at No. 7 Huabao Fang, Huanghe Road, led his accomplices, three people claiming to be special detectives surnamed Jiang and Wang, rushed in and claimed to be searching for red pills. On the bed in the room behind the sitting room where Chen was sitting, they found a pistol and handcuffs and threatened and extorted Chen. As a result, Hu and others pointed out Bao Songqing (50 years old this year, previously worked at the Gold Exchange), a fellow villager living at No. 5 Yong'anli, Baishang Road, and ordered Xin's wife, Jiangshi, to invite Bao to come, extorting 700 yuan. Jiang escorted Chen to Ningbo on the Xinjiangtian wheel. Later, after Chen returned to Shanghai, he was dissatisfied with Bao's collusion and reported it to the French Police. Detectives were sent to arrest Hu and others, but they had all fled. Only Bao was arrested and sent to the Second Special Zone Court for interrogation and investigation. All the details have been reported in the previous newspaper. Yesterday morning, presiding judge Wang Gangxu continued the trial in the Criminal Court 1. First, Yao Zhaodi, the lawyer for the police station, stated the police station's investigation process. Then, the plaintiff Chen Hesong recounted the experience of being defrauded and said that Bao and a man surnamed Wang had secretly whispered outside the door twice, which was obviously collusion. He now seeks to recover the defrauded money from Bao.

Bao Songqing confessed that he was at home that day when Xin Jiangshi, that is, Lao Erlian, came twice to ask me to intercede. I could not refuse because of the friendship with my fellow villager, so I went to mediate. I only nodded and recognized a man surnamed Wang, and I didn't know the man surnamed Jiang. Wang said that Jiang was a special detective and that Chen Hesong had a hundred guns and bullets to take back for the security corps. They were found and were going to be taken to the police station. They wanted me to intercede. I only said to give 200 yuan, but they didn't agree. Later, Chen himself agreed to give 700 yuan. Then Chen and Jiang went to get the money. When they came back, they put it on the table. I didn't touch it. Later, because Chen was carrying guns and bullets, he was afraid of inconvenience on the road, so he asked Jiang to accompany him to the ship. I went home and there was no collusion.

Xin Jiangshi, the witness, testified that at first she saw a big man with handcuffs in his hand, and also saw a bag, but didn't know what it was. Hu Quanhai ordered me to invite Bao Songqing to mediate. After the court verified the confession, it ordered the debate to begin, then announced the end of the session, and scheduled the sentence to be pronounced on the 9th. The defendant was ordered to submit a 2,000 yuan store bond to await the verdict.

Before Li Minzhou was Assassinated

The Assassin Loitered in the Corridor for a Long Time 142

The New New Company Believes it was Premeditated

The First Special Court Takes Testimony from Witnesses. Li Minzhou, the general manager of the New New Company, was shot and killed by Zhou Zhanyuan, the head of the store's security team, a native of Tianjin, in room 327 of the New New Hotel at 5:15 p.m. on the 1st of this month. Details have been reported in this newspaper. Yesterday morning, this case was continued in the First Criminal Court by Judge Feng Shide. Li Minzhou's family and lawyer Ting Lian Ting Rui were present in court. The defendant also hired two lawyers, Wei and Tan, to defend him. Lawyer Chen began by stating that the police's indictment of the defendant on charges of premeditated murder was quite appropriate. The New New Company is currently collecting evidence to prove that Zhou Zhanyuan's crime was premeditated. However, due to being busy with funeral arrangements for the past few days, they have not been able to complete the collection of evidence. He requested permission for a postponement. The police lawyer, Li Zhishan, continued by stating that since the postponement, the police had found two witnesses, Mr. Liu and Ge Chen Liangbin (both tea boys at the New New Hotel), who testified that before the incident, the defendant had been loitering in the hotel corridor for quite some time. The handgun used in the crime has been sent to the gun inspection bureau for examination. The examination report has not yet been received, so he requested a postponement. The court then questioned Zhou Zhanyuan, whose testimony remained the same as before. Chen Wenchuh, the deputy general manager of the New New Company, testified that he was unaware that the defendant possessed a handgun. Zhou had failed to lock the main door properly on October 29, 1930, which resulted in a major demerit. On May 2, 1933, he was given another demerit for failing to assign personnel for patrol. On October 26 of the same year, he was also given a demerit. This time, he was dismissed by Li because Zhou had failed to lock the front door. The two tea boys, Liu and Chen, testified that Zhou Zhanyuan had been pacing in the corridor with his head down before going to room 327. Not five minutes later, they heard a gunshot. Zhu Deren, the head of the security team, testified that Li Minzhou had ordered Zhou to hand over the keys, uniform, and police whistle to him. He then handed them over to him. Zhou claimed that he could not hand over the uniform until the next day because he had not brought his casual clothes. At that moment, he suddenly recalled that when Liu Xiji was the general manager, he had given Zhou a handgun. He then asked Zhou for it. Zhou replied that it was at home and would also hand it over the next day. This statement was heard by employee Xiao Zhaobin. However, Zhou denied that Zhu had asked him for the handgun. The court then summoned Xiao to the case. According to Xiao's testimony, he and Zhu were supervising Zhou's removal of his belongings when he did not hear Zhu mention the handgun. Later, when he was in the secretary's office, Zhu rushed in and said that Zhou had another gun that he would hand over the next day. He told Zhu that since he had a handgun, he should hand it over immediately. After the police lawyer and the defendant's lawyer cross-examined each witness, it was past noon. Judge Feng then ordered a postponement for further questioning.

A Huge Fire at Dapu Bridge Last Night Destroyed Over a Hundred Thatched Huts 143

=The fire was still not completely extinguished late into the night=

=And also affected more than ten tiled houses= Over a hundred thatched huts in the west of Dapu Bridge in the Nanshi area, inhabited mostly by poor workers, rickshaw pullers, and coolies from Jiangbei, suddenly caught fire around 9:10 p.m. last night. The fire spread rapidly and uncontrollably. Although the Nanshi district fire brigades rushed to the scene and tried their best to extinguish the fire, the wind was very strong and the fire was extremely fierce at the time, and the thatched huts were densely packed together, making it impossible to spray water effectively. The fire continued to burn until around 11 p.m. late into the night and had not been completely extinguished. As a result, more than ten tiled houses were also affected. The Second District Headquarters dispatched a large number of police officers to maintain order. The scene was filled with the cries of the old and young, a tragic sight that broke the heart.

Impersonating Lu Ying's Disciple 144

Zhang Qiufu Extorted Money and Was Arrested. Zhang Xixi, a merchant from No. 856 Fangbang Road, Chengnai, 30 years old, from Zhenjiang, who has been running a secondhand goods store for many years, reported to the leader of the district detective team, Liu Shaoqing, and the deputy leader, Wu Kezhong, of the Second District Police Department yesterday. Because he was timid, he asked his neighbor, Xu Dongbao, to come out and talk to him. Zhang Qiufu said that he was a student of team leader Lu and that they had stolen water pipes worth more than 800 yuan, so he had to compensate them 250 yuan. Xu Dongbao repeatedly tried to dissuade him without success, so he came to report it. Witness Chen Dongbao's testimony corroborated the plaintiff's statement. It was confirmed that the impersonator Zhang Qiufu falsely claimed to be a student of team leader Lu, spreading rumors and extorting money, which was extremely illegal and should be severely punished according to the law. Therefore, a document was prepared and sent to the General Bureau for further investigation by the Third Section.

After Zheng Mingshan's Death, His Brother and Wife Became Involved in a Lawsuit 148

=Mingshan Had No Heir, So His Brother's Son Inherited=

=The Brother Accused His Sister-in-Law of Embezzling the Inheritance=

=Now Mingshan's Wife is Suing Her Brother for False Accusation= The Rongyang and Gongzu socks factories were founded by Zheng Fengshan and Zheng Mingshan, brothers. The business was thriving and profitable. However, Mingshan, although in his prime, had no children. Therefore, he adopted Baiquan, the son of his brother Fengshan, as his heir. Unexpectedly, Mingshan suddenly fell ill and passed away two years ago. All of his inheritance was legally inherited by his wife, Zheng Yu Jingxiu, and his adopted son, Baiquan. At that time, because Baiquan was young, Zheng Yu Jingxiu, as his mother, was also his legal guardian and manager of the assets under Baiquan's name. Unexpectedly, Zheng Fengshan suddenly filed a criminal lawsuit with the First Special District Court last year, accusing Zheng Yu Jingxiu of embezzling the inheritance. The Special Court held a hearing and summoned her, but because Zheng Fengshan was not qualified, the court ruled that it would not accept the case. However, Zheng Yu Jingxiu felt aggrieved by the unfounded lawsuit and hired two lawyers, Chen Tingrui and Sun Zuji, to file a lawsuit against Zheng Fengshan for false accusation in the First Special District Court. The main points of her lawsuit were as follows: In the previous case where Zheng Fengshan sued the plaintiff for embezzlement in the court, his statement alleged that the plaintiff was naturally superstitious and extremely wasteful, spending extravagantly without regard for the cost. After receiving the inheritance, she abused her rights at will, disposed of the assets without authorization, and secretly colluded with Yu Xifan, now the general manager of the two factories, allowing him to wield power alone and manage them improperly, causing losses. She also secretly mortgaged all the assets under different names, with cunning schemes and cruel methods. All of these allegations were fabricated. The plaintiff's family has always been frugal, and she has not secretly disposed of the assets under different names. Even if she had, it would be an inherent right of the owner. Moreover, what he said was not true. Yu Xifan is currently the assistant manager of the Gongzu Socks Factory, elected by the shareholders, and not the general manager of the two factories. The defendant was aware of these facts but wanted to illegally seize the property rights, fabricating baseless accusations and filing a lawsuit for embezzlement with the intention of causing others to be criminally punished. He had committed a crime under Article 180, Paragraph 1 of the Criminal Law and should be severely punished. The court approved the request and ordered a collective hearing in the Second Criminal Court yesterday afternoon, presided over by Judge Wu Zehan. The plaintiff Zheng Yu Jingxiu was represented by two lawyers, Chen and Sun, while the defendant Zheng Fengshan was absent, and his lawyer, Jiang Yiping, stated that Zheng had left Shanghai due to important matters and requested a postponement. Judge Wu granted the postponement for seven days, pending the defendant's appearance in court for further verification.

The Situation of Various Parks in the Public Concession 150

=A Total of More Than 3.39 Million Visitors=

=An Increase of 1.26 Million Compared to the Previous Year=

The report on the work of the director of the Parks Management Office of the Municipal Council for the past year stated that the areas of the parks that were expanded this year included the northeastern part of Hongkou Park. After renovation, more than ten ball fields were added. The land at the western end of Jiaozhou Road Park was slightly repaired using materials from the dismantled Singapore Road Park.

Hongkou Park: This year, the total number of visitors to Hongkou Park was 1,178,293, an increase of more than 392,000 compared to the previous year and more than 568,000 compared to the year before. The day with the most visitors was July 16, with 46,209 people, breaking all previous records. The new constructions in the park included several stone statues, transplanted next to the rest hall, and a chain fence added to the flower bed opposite the Bailinan Road Park gate. A summer pavilion, five drinking fountains, and two restrooms were built in the park, and trees were planted. The chrysanthemum and dahlia exhibitions were praised by botanists. The zoo section was often crowded on weekends. More than 70 birds and animals were donated and purchased.

Hongkou Park: This park rebuilt 3 stone bridges, filled in a small pond, repaired several sections of the pond bank, and added four drinking fountains. The sports facilities included football, basketball, baseball, team ball, grass field, and hard court tennis courts. In addition, there were golf courses, fishing areas, and track and field venues.

Huishan Park: This park has been attracting more attention year by year. This year, a flower garden was created on the site of the lotus pond and redecorated. A section of the walkway was paved with cement. Grass field and grass tennis courts were also popular.

Bund Park: Stone walls have been built around the flower beds and trees have been planted to provide protection. The environment of this park is not very suitable for flowers, but this year's flower exhibition was still noteworthy.

Children's Playground: The Kunshan Road square in the children's playground was always full of people, making it difficult to maintain the lawn in good condition. The Nanyang Road playground was redesigned, with raised lawns, repaired roads, built grass huts, and transplanted trees. Too many adults entered Singapore Park, which interfered with children's play. A part of the park is currently being used to build a Chinese girls' middle school, so there have been slight changes to the park. To maintain the tranquility of the children's games, efforts have been made to restrict pedestrians from passing through Zhoushan Park. The Suzhou Road playground was also very popular.

Open-Air Music: Last year, 29 orchestral concerts, 31 brass band concerts, 4 military band concerts, and 12 military performances (retirement songs) were held in various parks. On average, 108 people attended each afternoon concert and 367 people attended each evening concert.

Visitor Statistics

Last year, in addition to 1,178,293 visitors to Hongkou Park, Hongkou Park had 904,917 visitors, Bund Park had 652,134 visitors, and other parks and children's playgrounds had 661,525 visitors, for a total of 3,396,869 visitors, an increase of 1,268,684 compared to the previous year.

The Municipal Public Security Bureau Strictly Forbids Impersonation and Collection of Festival Fees 151

The Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau sent a letter to this newspaper yesterday, stating: "According to a report from the Third Precinct of the First District, (it has been found that someone within the district is holding a receipt from a certain precinct of the Household Registration Department of the Public Security Bureau and collecting festival fees of two dimes per household. After the precinct chief received the report, he immediately dispatched police officers from the precinct to investigate door-to-door. More than ten households have already been charged. In addition to informing each household to report to the police if anyone impersonates them to collect festival fees in the future, and ordering the precinct to pay attention to investigating and punishing them, it is feared that similar incidents may occur in other districts. Therefore, a document is submitted, along with eight receipts, for the director's review and to order the precincts to handle the matter), etc. In response, in addition to issuing a general order for strict investigation and separate letters, a copy of the original fake receipts is enclosed for your review and to publish it in the news column so that citizens are aware. If the fraudulent offender is found, immediately hand them over to the local police for transfer to the bureau for investigation."

Rental Dispute on Waima Road, Wusong 153

Various Organizations Consult and Mediate

Several hundred houses on Waima Road in Wusong Town, all owned by Renchanghe Company, were destroyed in the war. A portion of the houses has been completed. However, a major dispute has arisen regarding the rental of houses between new and old tenants. The general old tenants have organized the "Resident United Benefit Association," petitioning various authorities in Wusong to appeal and demand: (1) Old tenants have priority in renting; (2) Rent increases shall not exceed 20% of the original rent; (3) Security deposits shall comply with the regulations promulgated by the Municipal Government; (4) Abolish illegal exactions such as "small rent digging fees." Although the houses have been completed, neither new nor old tenants can move in for the time being. Wusong authorities believe that the houses on Waima Road are of great importance to the development of business in the city and fear that the dispute will escalate, hindering social security. Yesterday afternoon at 1:00 PM, the 7th District Public Security Bureau discussed solutions. Municipal Committee member Tang Chengzong, Chamber of Commerce Chairman Zhang Yuci, Party Department members Wang Cheng'e, Wu Renji, 7th District Officer Yin Gongtian, and others consulted and decided: (1) Regarding illegal exactions such as small rents, the Party Department will investigate and the Public Security Bureau will handle the case; (2) It was decided to convene representatives of landlords and tenants at the Wusong Municipal Office at 1:00 PM on the 8th of this month for mediation.

The Truth About Patriotic Female Teacher Huang Shuiqing's Suicide Attempt 155

=Unrelated to Love or Economics, Suicide Attempt is Also First Time=

=Resentful of Treatment by Current Principal, She Attempts Suicide in Anger= Ms. Huang Shan (also known as Bingqing), a teacher at the Patriotic Girls' School, came to Shanghai on the 1st of this month and stayed at the Xinhuizhong Hotel. She took sleeping pills in an attempt to commit suicide. The waiter discovered her and sent her to Renji Hospital for treatment. Details were briefly reported in yesterday's newspaper. Shanghai reporters conducted separate investigations to clarify the truth. The details are as follows: The Cause of Suicide

Ms. Huang is a Minhang native. She graduated from Beijing Women's Normal School. Because she liked sports, she entered the physical education department of the Patriotic Girls' School. After graduation, she continued to serve at her alma mater. She was highly valued by former principals Ji Rongwu and Ji Yisheng for her capable handling of affairs. After Sun Xiangzhong became principal the year before last, she once worked at schools such as Anhui Second Women's School. Later, Principal Sun repeatedly wrote letters to her, urging her to serve at her alma mater, with an agreed that with one patriotic day, Bingqing would be at the Patriotic school for one day). The words were sincere, so Ms. Huang returned to Shanghai to serve as the head of the Girl Scout troop and a physical education teacher at her alma mater. She was extremely responsible for school affairs. For example, when the January 28th Incident broke out, the school was located in the war zone, which was extremely dangerous. The principal, teachers, and staff all fled. Nearby students went home, while more than 20 students from far away were led by Ms. Huang Shan and Ms. Wei Yunqing to take refuge in Moore Hall. They joined the Girl Scout battlefield service group, serving the community on the one hand and taking care of their classmates on the other. After the war subsided, the school rented temporary school buildings in Continental Village. Huang returned to the school, but the school was economically exhausted due to the damage from the Shanghai War. When salaries were not paid, Huang still endured hardships and worked diligently, maintaining the school for a semester. Whenever there were sports meets or Girl Scout inspections, even when she was sick, she still made efforts to serve the public. Her efforts to serve her alma mater can be seen from this.

Suicide Attempt and Rescue During this year's winter vacation, Huang took a vacation to Hangzhou and stayed with her sister, Huang Lian, waiting for school to start. Unexpectedly, on January 17th, she received a letter from Principal Sun, using the excuse of the school's financial difficulties and wanting to reduce her salary. The words not only did not mention her past merits but also used sophisticated methods to satirize her. After reading the letter, Ms. Huang recalled the past and was filled with grief and indignation. Her sister then wrote a reply on her behalf, questioning Principal Sun. On the 24th, she received another reply from Principal Sun, which made Ms. Huang even more embarrassed. Therefore, her sister wrote a second letter refuting him. After this, Ms. Huang cried all day, even staying up late at night. Her sister was deeply worried. On February 1st, Huang took advantage of her sister and brother-in-law being out for work to leave a note and come to Shanghai, staying at the Huizhong Hotel. Her brother-in-law, Mr. Ge, tracked her to Shanghai and searched everywhere, but there was no news. Until the morning before yesterday, the hotel waiter discovered that Ms. Huang had taken sleeping pills in an attempt to commit suicide. The police sent her to Renji Hospital. Fortunately, it was discovered early, and she was rescued and survived.

Interview Process Yesterday, Ms. Huang moved into Tongde Hospital. The reporter visited her at the hospital and saw that she was lying peacefully on the bed and was conscious. However, she still resented Sun Xiangzhong very much and occasionally complained. Ms. Huang's father and sisters were taking care of her by her side. The reporter felt that Ms. Huang was too stimulated and did not want to talk too much, so her sister, Huang Lian, reported the truth about the suicide to the reporter, saying that rumors of a second suicide were completely false. The family's economic situation was still relatively affluent, and there was no relationship with love. Huang's suicide was entirely due to Sun Xiangzhong's disregard for past kindness, inviting her to come and dismissing her, which caused her to be stimulated.
