Incoming 163

The Current Cigarette Tax Rate is the Same for the Government and Chinese Merchants 164

Request to the Government for Detailed Reconsideration and Prompt Improvement of Losses (Continued) by Huang Ziping

However, this is only in regard to the cigarette industry. If we discuss native tobacco leaves, the losses are also quite significant. Lower-grade cigarettes are entirely made from native leaves, and because the tax on lower-grade cigarettes is heavy and thus uncompetitive, the sales of native tobacco leaves will inevitably stagnate as well. According to statistics from the People's Cigarette Company and other sources, the annual sales of native tobacco leaves produced in areas such as Susong, Huanggang, Xinchang, Dengzhou, Champion, Guangshui, and Junzhou were approximately 390,000 bales under the seven-tier tax system before 1930. After the implementation of the three-tier tax system in November 1930, this figure decreased to 260,000 bales. After the implementation of the two-tier tax system in 1932, it further decreased to 115,000 bales. Recently, with the tax reform, it is said that these tobacco leaves are almost ignored. The Tax Bureaus in Jiujiang and Laohekou have established native tobacco offices and it is requested to forward letters to the Tax Bureau ordering them to investigate and report back, which will surely reveal the truth. Under the current tax system, the tax on native tobacco is four yuan, one jiao, and four fen per hundred jin. If this leads to a decline in sales, what will be the government's loss in tax revenue? What will be the loss to the rural areas as tobacco farmers go bankrupt? These are figures that cannot be calculated. All of this is closely related to the foundation of the nation and the national economy. Those who set tax rates must consider the importance of China and the Chinese nation and take all of this into account. It is believed that the error of the two-tier tax system lies entirely in the tax reduction for high-grade cigarettes and the tax increase for lower-grade cigarettes. High-grade cigarettes are expensive, while lower-grade cigarettes are cheap. Under the seven-tier tax system, the selling price of a carton of high-grade cigarettes was 1,052 yuan, with a tax of 404 yuan. The selling price of a carton of seven-grade cigarettes was 125 yuan, with a tax of 29 yuan. This adheres to the principle of tax averaging, taxing according to value. The tax on one carton of high-grade cigarettes is more than enough to offset the tax on a dozen cartons of lower-grade cigarettes. Therefore, to ensure sufficient tax revenue, one must treat high, medium, and low-grade cigarettes equally, and not focus solely on lower-grade cigarettes. Let us assume that the government must raise 3.8 million yuan in additional cigarette taxes. If this burden is not placed solely on the lower-grade cigarettes of Chinese merchants, but also shared by the high-grade cigarettes of British and American merchants, then, as a concession, let each bear half the burden. Chinese merchants would only need to bear an additional 1.9 million yuan. Why should they bear the heavy tax of over 14 million yuan? If it is said that regardless of the people's ability to bear the burden, Chinese merchants must bear an additional 14 million yuan in taxes, and British and American merchants should bear the same amount, then, since the sales volume of British and American cigarettes is greater than that of Chinese merchants, and what they sell is the expensive high-grade cigarettes, taxing according to value, the tax payments of British and American merchants will simultaneously increase by more than 30 million yuan. The government's revenue, combined, could increase by 50 million yuan annually. Therefore, for the sake of increasing tax revenue, the government must impose the same tax on high, medium, and low-grade cigarettes. The logic is very simple. Under the two-tier tax system, the tax on lower-grade cigarettes is excessively high, while the tax rate on high-grade cigarettes is too low, only causing endless losses to Chinese merchants and allowing British and American merchants to reap huge profits. It can truly be said to have a hundred harms and not a single benefit. However, this is still in regard to the two-tier tax system of 1932. Under the current two-tier tax system, first-grade cigarettes are almost non-existent, practically zero. What is actually collected is only the second grade, which is essentially a one-tier tax. The tax on lower-grade cigarettes has increased from 55 yuan per carton to 80 yuan per carton, an even greater increase than before. The tax on high-grade cigarettes has decreased from 95 yuan per carton to 80 yuan per carton, an even greater decrease than before. It has not been implemented for long, and the losses to Chinese merchants and the profits to British and American merchants have not been clearly statistically quantified. However, based on previous methods of calculation, the losses to Chinese merchants are likely to be over 20 million yuan annually, and the profits to British and American merchants are at least 16 or 17 million yuan. If it is continued to be implemented, these remaining forty or fifty Chinese merchants will inevitably go bankrupt one after another, and all domestic native tobacco leaves will be eliminated. Tobacco farmers in Hubei, Jiangxi, and Anhui will subsequently go bankrupt. Alas, the government is supposed to be a government for the people. It would not bear to be a tool of the British and Americans, killing off Chinese merchants and tobacco farmers, and sacrificing domestic native tobacco leaves and tobacco taxes as funeral objects, allowing British and American merchants to sit back and suck the marrow of 16 or 17 million yuan annually from Chinese merchants. Therefore, it is urgent to rise up and immediately abolish it, without allowing any hesitation. Some may say that, as mentioned above, the current tax system, with a tax of 80 yuan per carton on lower-grade cigarettes, and a discretionary increase on high and medium-grade cigarettes according to their grade, is a brilliant way to raise funds. However, it is believed that this is not the case. A tax of 80 yuan per carton on lower-grade cigarettes is a heavy tax of 120% of the value, which the people cannot afford at this time. The recent bankruptcies of Chinese merchants are the result of the unbearable heavy tax on lower-grade cigarettes. If high and medium-grade cigarettes are also taxed at 120% of their value, it will lead to the ruin of the entire cigarette industry, causing the government and cigarette merchants to suffer together. There is no way this can be done. The only solution is to adopt the principle of equal burden for high, medium, and low-grade cigarettes, and to set the tax rate at a moderate level. The newly set two-tier tax rates, with 36% of the value for high-grade cigarettes and 120% of the value for low-grade cigarettes, are both too low and too high. If they are moderately revised to a uniform 50% to 60% of the value, the burden on cigarette merchants will be more fair, and the government's tax revenue, although reduced for lower-grade cigarettes, will greatly increase for high and medium-grade cigarettes, which will benefit the national treasury. The association does not have accurate records of the selling prices and sales volumes of various cigarette brands, and the government has not published them. Ziping and others have no basis for calculating. The Tax Bureau should have detailed registrations. If the discussion is based on this principle, a proper reading and response can surely be determined.

On Studying Language 165

Reading Guidance: The discontinuation of the Shenbao reader advisory column filled me with endless melancholy! Now, the establishment of reading guidance fills me with boundless joy! Indeed, reading the reading questions and answers for the past few days has increased my knowledge significantly. However, my questions are not similar to those, and everyone has their own reading plan. Therefore, I am taking advantage of this only one hour to write this (My One-Year Reading Plan) for the consideration of you gentlemen. I am a knowledge-starved person, deeply feeling the pain of insufficient vocabulary. When I pick up a pen, I cannot express my own meaning; when I pick up a book, I cannot understand anything slightly deeper. Therefore, I do not dare to blindly study anything. I only strive to practice (Chinese at a level above beginner). For clarity, I will elaborate on my situation below.

My Environment: I am currently an apprentice in a store in a small town. Although I do not even have an hour of time each day, I have made up my mind to quit this trade after the Lunar New Year. (The reason for quitting: I labor all day, all month, and all year, and the reward is only thirty yuan a year! Moreover, there is no good future in this. Because I cannot find a suitable occupation for the time being, I plan to use this (One-Year Reading Plan) to return to my hometown and study on my own for a year. Fortunately, my family can still afford my food and clothing.) At that time, I will have ample time, a quiet life, and be able to focus on self-study, which I will definitely be able to do.

My Level: I attended junior high school for one semester, and then fell into this trap: the store. Although I have read many novels, both old and new, I have only glanced at them and have not read most of them carefully. I cannot understand classical Chinese without annotations, and modern poetry is too new and I do not understand it. For example, I am not qualified to appreciate the poetry of modernism. It is shameful to say, but my Chinese seems to have no foundation. However, I am still young (eighteen years old this year). As long as I can work hard, I can always achieve my hopes, right?

My Hopes: I do not hope to become a writer (this is a dream). I only hope that I can understand all ancient books and appreciate poetry such as modernism; when I pick up a pen, I can express my meaning as I wish. In short, I only hope to become someone who is (above the basic level in Chinese).

One-Year Reading Plan: Select and read one classical Chinese article every day, and read it thoroughly. Read a certain number of pages of books (ancient or new; specify how many books to read in a year). In addition, subscribe to one magazine and one newspaper. Practice writing a certain amount every day, and write several essays every week. All of this is specified. This is my one-year plan. As for whether this can achieve my hopes, that is another matter, because this is only the first stage of my plan.

I can only write such a superficial plan as above. Really, I cannot write any better. I hope that the teacher can revise it or provide another (One-Year Self-Study Curriculum). In this letter, there are many questions that I will write down together: (1) For someone like me, are my hopes too extravagant? (2) What classical Chinese should I read? What books should I read? (Please provide a detailed list.) (3) What kind of essays should I write? Is it okay to write novels? (4) Is it beneficial to join the Commercial Press Correspondence School? (5) What books should I read more of? What books are most suitable for me? (Specify a range to avoid being lost in the vast sea of learning.) I hope the above five questions can be answered together. I deeply hope that the teacher's revised plan can guide me into a regulated reading process, approaching with a certain purpose and following a predetermined step-by-step approach.

I deeply await it here. (Letter from Cheng Keying) Corrections: 1. Yesterday's title should be changed to (The Logic of Reading). 2. The name Li Siqi should be in parentheses ( ) and the words (Letter) should be added. 3. In the first line of the third column, the (,) after (and) should be removed and a (个) should be added to become (an individual's purpose...)

Spring and Autumn

Winter Vacation 166

— Yan

I remember that winter vacation was two weeks long, from January 18th to 31st, which was stipulated by the Ministry of Education, for all universities, middle schools, and primary schools. In some years, these two weeks coincided with the end and beginning of the Lunar New Year, but this year is unlucky. The new semester begins on February 1st, which is only the 18th day of the twelfth lunar month. This means that school will start on the 18th day of the twelfth lunar month, and classes will be held on the first day of the Lunar New Year. Therefore, this year's winter vacation for various schools has undergone a major and special change, regardless of violating the orders of the Ministry of Education or the Bureau of Education. Not to mention the rural schools, even if the teachers do not take a Lunar New Year vacation, the students will still give the teachers a vacation. In Shanghai, some universities take a month off, from the end of the Lunar New Year to the beginning of the new year; some middle schools take three weeks off, from mid-January to mid-February; some primary schools start school on the 27th or 28th day of the twelfth lunar month, and the most common is starting school at the end of the Lunar New Year. Those who start school after the Lunar New Year reason that society still celebrates the Lunar New Year, everyone is busy preparing for the New Year at the end of the year, and everyone is desperately short of money. If school starts within the year, where will the students get the money to pay all the tuition and board fees? They are considerate of the fact that students' parents have difficulty raising funds within the year, and they are unwilling to let students enter school and pay fees after the New Year, fearing that they will not receive their fees after they enter school. Those who start school at the end of the year do so because the first week of school cannot actually be used for classes. It is nominally starting school within the year, but in reality, it is equivalent to taking off the first day of the Lunar New Year. Even the students will definitely not come to school at the end of the year. On the one hand, school is considered to have started within the year, which also counts as not violating the orders of the superiors. This method is the most clever.

Although the dates for winter vacation are stipulated, the various schools are giving vacations in such a colorful variety of ways. I do not know how the competent authorities will maintain their prestige. But looking at it broadly, what can be done to ensure that orders are followed and prestige is maintained? This extremely ordinary matter of winter vacation is being dealt with carelessly. What does it matter?

Refuting Rumors 167

— Xianxian

The third young lady of the Yang Mansion lives in seclusion in her boudoir and rarely goes out. Although everyone does not mention her name very often, whenever her name is mentioned, everyone admits that she is as pure as ice and jade. However, recently, rumors have suddenly spread that on a certain day in a certain month, Miss Yang III had a secret rendezvous with someone at a certain place. This matter is a castle in the air and not worth believing. If the accused dismisses it with a laugh, the rumors will soon be stopped by the wise and no one will talk about it anymore. But Miss Yang III insisted on publicly refuting the rumors in the newspaper and at the same time pursued the rumor-mongers through legal procedures. Such a commotion will surely cause a sensation throughout the city, known to women and children. Although there will eventually be a day when the truth comes out, it will inevitably leave a very deep and bad impression in the minds of people. Some people even speculate that Miss Yang III may have done such a thing, otherwise, the pure would be pure and the impure would be impure, why make such a fuss?

Logically, refuting rumors is naturally a legitimate procedure, but in this day and age, rumors have changed somewhat and are like a mischievous child. Modern educators do not advocate whipping children, especially mischievous children. Indeed, we can often see impatient mothers whipping mischievous children. The more they whip, the more mischievous the children become. Mothers who understand the principles of education always patiently guide their children and can educate them well. Rumors are also like this. For example, the story of Miss Yang III mentioned above. If Miss Yang III treats the baseless rumors as a mischievous child and simply shows people her pure and jade-like facts, the rumors will be defeated without being attacked.

In Shanghai, some people are kidnapped by kidnappers. When newspaper reporters go to the address to interview, the family members of the kidnapped people shake their heads and deny that such a thing happened. Naturally, this makes it difficult for the news to spread. This achieves the opposite effect compared to formally refuting rumors. This is a spirit worth admiring.

Jenga's Random Thoughts 168

— Yan Jenga

Plan

(Plan) and (Hope) are different, hope is always an empty fantasy, but a plan has the possibility of being realized.

(A year's plan lies in spring, a day's plan lies in morning). This way, people have already determined their plans ahead of time.

If we compare people to vehicles, then the plan is the track. With a stable track, we can drive safely. It can be seen that, regardless of whether the matter is big or small, there should be a precise plan. Although the plan may not be fully realized, it can at least reduce the components of failure.

Environment

The environment is created by people, but people hate the environment, so there is an extreme contradiction!

For example, people who live in the city, on the one hand, they curse the city, on the other hand, they are obsessed with the city, they are not satisfied with the current environment, and they cannot summon the courage to transform the environment!

We believe that the environment can change people, but it can only change people with weak wills; people with strong wills can overcome adverse environments everywhere.

Friends: Let us be a team of soldiers fighting the environment!

Experience

In the great universe, there are all kinds of phenomena; in the process of life, there are all kinds of tastes; only experience can taste all kinds of tastes from this great universe.

A scientist can invent unprecedented physics, a philosopher can utter amazing remarks, an artist can write beautiful poems or draw pictures... these all come from experience, who can say that experience is nosy?

The great Russian writer Turgenev, he was willing to give up aristocratic life to be a vagrant, and he finally obtained a great career through the experience of wandering.

Therefore, experience is not only a kind of intimate lesson, but also a ladder to success.

Short Message 169

The New Shanghai magazine, published by the Hurbina Publishing House in Donghua Lane, Simalu, is unique and divided into three major parts, edited by Wang Tianhen, Hu Xiongsheng, and Chen Liufeng. The part edited by Wang is responsible for translations, with Zhou Shoujuan, Yan Duhe, Zhao Shaokang, Cheng Xiaoqing, Cheng Zhanlu, etc. as translators.

The part edited by Hu is responsible for translations, with Zhang Ziping, Mu Shiying, Gao Ming, Jin Mancheng, Wang Xinming, etc. as translators. The part edited by Chen is for pictures, divided into photos, pictures, and New Shanghai comics, with Yang Qingpan, Ding Song, etc. as authors. Moreover, they are not nominal, and all publish their own satisfactory works in the magazine, so they are full of spirit and very different from ordinary. The first edition of the first issue was 10,000 copies, which were sold out in less than a month, and now it has been reprinted.

The subsequent issues also have remaining books. The retail price is three corners per issue, and the annual subscription is three yuan and five corners.

Northeast Fourth Company Commander 170

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter 24: Drinking and Eating Together, a Wild Farewell Feast Full of Tears; Burning the Midnight Oil and Dreaming, Singing Softly Through the Long Night.

He said this very naturally, but when Ziqiang heard it, he felt that every word was like a needle, stabbing into his heart. Although he wanted to use a few words to comfort Guizhi in his heart, his tongue would not obey his command, and he could not say a word. The Jiang family saw him standing there stiffly, his hands hanging straight down, as if he was standing at attention with his new wife, so she said to him: Son-in-law, don't worry. We are not so ignorant. Since you have returned on leave, you still have official duties to attend to. You can take care of it yourself.

You should leave today if you should leave today. If you can delay it for another day, it will be easier to leave tomorrow. Old man, what do you think of my words? Saying this, she turned her face to Zhao Weng. Zhao Weng said: Dear lady, your words show how much you care for your son-in-law. What else can our children say? Ziqiang, I don't think you can leave today. Fortunately, although the telegram has arrived, it has not specified which day you have to arrive by. Relatively speaking, if you want to be more relaxed, you should leave tomorrow. Ziqiang then opened his mouth and said: Yes, I have also calculated that the car will enter the city at 6:30 tomorrow morning, catching the 8:00 train to Shanhaiguan at the East Station. I will get off at Luanzhou and go back by land. Zhao Weng said: That's up to you. As he spoke, his hand kept rising and wiping down the newspaper, as if this action could relieve the depression in his heart. The Jiang family said to Guizhi: Go home and sit down. He heard this and followed his mother back home. Ziqiang said to Zhao Weng: As far as I can see, there is nothing going on at the front, it's just that Battalion Commander Bao can't do without me. Zhao Weng said: But the rules in the military camp, except for the front line when the fighting is on, as long as you apply for a marriage leave, you can always get it approved. Why did he send you a telegram to urge you before your leave was over? I'm afraid there are some reasons in this? How could Ziqiang dare to say that there was a reason? He stood still and did not say anything. (239)

The Three Friends of Winter 171

— Yu Youqing

Pine, bamboo, and plum are the three friends of winter. A few days ago, Suzhou was covered in snow, which was the day when the three friends of winter were in the limelight. In the vast expanse of white, there were green pines, green bamboos, and red plums, embellishing it, how beautiful it was!

The poets of the past praised the maple leaves, saying that they were more beautiful than the flowers of February. However, when the year is coming to an end, the pine, bamboo, and plum trees show off their beauty even more beautifully than the maple leaves by ten times.

The ancients compared the pine to a doctor, but I compare it to a loyal and brave man, unchanging in his integrity. I often say that the 19th Route Army in the January 28th Incident was as stubborn as a pine tree, not afraid of the bullying of strong neighbors, just like the pine tree in the snow, revealing its heroic posture. Since the Fujian Incident, I feel that the 19th Route Army is not as unchanging in its integrity and stubborn to the end as the pine tree.

The ancients compared bamboo to a gentleman, but I compare it to a talented man who is unappreciated. In ordinary times, his true talent and practical knowledge cannot be seen, and he does not show his abilities, burying himself for life. When the opportunity comes, Pang Tong is not just a talent for a hundred miles. What others cannot do, he can do everything. He is lonely and proud throughout his life, unloved, and preserves his original spirit, holding his embrace, untainted by dust. He is truly what Ruan Ji's madness is, how could he be a mere hawker? It is a pity that there are not many people who love bamboo and talent. The ancients compared plum to a beauty, but I compare it to a simple woman. In a depressed economy, it is rare to find a woman who values frugality. The so-called beauties of the times are nothing more than wild lions and wild cats! Chastity is not discussed, extravagance is valued, and the social atmosphere is getting worse and worse, with people deceiving each other.

I feel that the plum blossom is cold and fragrant, and lonely and proud, with no trace of fear. No wonder Lin Chushi loved it like a wife. Alas! In this vast world, how many people are like the pine, bamboo, and plum in the snow?

New Invention

Wine Contains Vitamin B2 172

Recently, Yamada Yutaka, a graduate student at the Osaka Municipal Hygiene Laboratory in Japan, under the guidance of Dr. Fujiwara Kuzujiro, the director of the laboratory, discovered new information in the chemical history of vitamins. As a result of his analysis and research on various types of wine, he discovered that wine contains vitamin B2. This vitamin B2 is a major component of nutrients for the human body. Because vitamin B can be divided into five types: 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5, vitamin 1 is rich in the function of preventing beriberi, and vitamin B has the effect of promoting the development of various parts of the body. Yamada's paper proves that the vitamin contained in wine is based on comparative experiments on several types of beer, wine, Japanese sake, and Shaoxing wine. The alcohol in Shaoxing wine is the least, but the vitamin content is the highest. Therefore, it is considered inappropriate to legally prohibit minors from drinking alcohol, because when they drink alcohol, their faces turn red, their ears turn warm, which is a manifestation of stimulating blood vessel expansion, which is also the effect of vitamin B2, which promotes the function of body development. Therefore, old Shaoxing wine has a great effect on people with neurasthenia and pale complexion. The various medicinal wines passed down by our Chinese people, in addition to the medicinal properties that can eliminate diseases, the greatest benefit to the body is the vitamin B2 in the wine. Mr. Yamada once carefully experimented with white rats and expressed his opinion. He said: Use 30 grams of white rats, use low temperature and low pressure to remove the alcohol and water in Japanese sake, beer, wine, and Shaoxing wine, so that it becomes a kind of concentrated liquid. If we add feed lacking vitamin B2 to feed the white rats, and compare it with the feed that does not add this concentrated liquid to feed the white rats, the results of their development show that the white rats that do not eat the concentrated liquid will die in less than 50 days, and the feed with the concentrated liquid of wine can live up to 87 days, and if you add beer, Japanese sake, and Shaoxing wine, it can survive to more than 100 days. Therefore, the weight of the white rats can reach 210 grams if the concentrated liquid of wine is added as feed, which proves that the vitamin B2 in wine has a great effect on developing and promoting the function of the body.

Kerosene Can Cure Lung Disease 173

— Bing Yu

Experiments on eating kerosene to treat lung disease have now been proven in both Eastern and Western countries. It was initially discovered in the case of a young woman who committed suicide, the daughter of a carriage business owner. She suffered from lung disease and,厌世, committed suicide.

She secretly drank a bottle of kerosene, believing she would bid farewell to the world forever. Unexpectedly, after drinking the kerosene, her lung disease was greatly alleviated, shocking society. Later, doctors began experimenting with kerosene, and it consistently proved effective. Moreover, it was determined that kerosene is highly effective for laryngeal tuberculosis, hemorrhoids, caries of the spine, and other forms of tuberculosis, as well as diabetes and asthma. Previously, scholars worldwide were aware of countless medications for lung disease, but they were all harmful rather than beneficial. Later, treatment methods emphasized rest, a change of environment for recovery, proper nourishment, and natural therapies such as absorbing fresh air. However, these methods could not fundamentally cure the disease. Now, after experiments on animals by renowned medical experts and chemists, kerosene has been recognized as an unparalleled remedy for eradicating tuberculosis. It is said that a capitalist in Okayama Prefecture, Japan, lived to the age of 113 because he regularly consumed kerosene. Among the workers at the Yamazumi Oil & Coal Company in Yamaguchi Prefecture, not a single person suffered from lung disease. The director of the Hyogo Prefectural Children's Research Institute, Dr. Torakazu Hayami, eradicated various diseases of the stomach, intestines, and kidneys by drinking 30 grams of kerosene in divided doses. When he dripped a drop of kerosene into a culture of tuberculosis bacteria, the bacteria were completely killed, demonstrating kerosene's strong antibacterial effect. He later experimented on rabbits and achieved remarkable results. A neighbor who had suffered from lung disease for ten years, with his lungs resembling a honeycomb and in the third and most dangerous stage, was completely cured in less than a month by drinking 15 grams of kerosene daily under his direction. The method of consumption varies depending on age and physical condition, but generally, one should start with 10 grams and not exceed 15 grams. The best time to drink it is 9 PM, without having eaten dinner. Drink it before going to bed at 9 PM, and repeat the dose in four or five days, then again in six or seven days. Gradually increasing the amount to 15 grams will naturally produce results. Therefore, scholars in various European countries now regard kerosene as a miraculous remedy for lung disease.

Undertaking the Revival of the Oriental Library 178

Organizing Domestic and International Sponsorship Committees to Collect Books. The Commercial Press Allocates Annual Public Welfare Funds as a Recovery Fund. Plans to Rebuild a Grand Site, Realizable in Five Years. The Oriental Library is the only cultural treasure in Asia. During the January 28th Incident, it was completely destroyed by Japanese artillery fire. The loss cannot be measured in money alone; it is a major catastrophe in the history of world culture. Considering the significant impact of the library's destruction on society and culture, Chinese and foreign cultural circles are actively pursuing its revival, organizing the Oriental Library Revival Committee, determining a revival plan, and having the Commercial Press allocate one-third of its annual public welfare funds as a recovery fund. Sponsorship committees are being organized in Germany, the United States, the United Kingdom, and France. Book collection agencies are being established in seven major cultural centers in China, including Nanjing and Beiping. As of recently, tens of thousands of volumes of books have been newly collected. A large number of books from France and Germany will also be shipped to Shanghai within the month. Plans are also being made to purchase land and build a new library in the central area of Jing'an Temple to restore its former glory. A reporter from the Shenshi News Agency visited Wang Yunwu, the general manager of the Commercial Press, yesterday and obtained detailed information about the library's revival plan and current progress, which are recorded as follows:

Before and After the Destruction The Oriental Library originated in the 30th year of the Guangxu reign of the Qing Dynasty and was officially established in the 13th year of the Republic of China. It was destroyed on January 29, 1932. The library's collection included 268,000 volumes of Chinese books and over 80,000 volumes of Western books, covering all essential reference books in various scientific disciplines, both ancient and modern, Chinese and foreign. There were over 5,000 types of charts, including films of books collected by the Roman Pope Vatican Palace, Empress Dowager, Queen, and Crown Prince of the Tang Dynasty at the end of the Ming Dynasty, along with their officials and converts to Catholicism. The collection of rare books included the Complete Library of the Four Branches of Literature, local chronicles, and three major categories of Chinese and foreign magazines and newspapers, which were particularly valuable. In addition, there were many volumes of Western ancient books printed before the 15th century, totaling 463,083 volumes. On January 29, 1932, the library was bombed and burned by Japanese aircraft, and the cultural collection accumulated over thirty years was reduced to ashes. The material loss exceeded one million yuan.

Undertaking the Revival After resuming business last year, the Commercial Press deeply felt that the destruction of the Oriental Library had a significant impact on Chinese social culture and scholarship. It immediately began planning its revival. Recently, the Oriental Library Revival Committee was organized, and revival steps and plans were drawn up and actively implemented. Hu Shi, Cai Yuanpei, Chen Guangfu, Zhang Jusheng, Wang Yunwu, and international scholars such as Geller from the United States, Oudemans from Germany, Zhang Xuelou from the United Kingdom, and Li Rong from France were appointed as committee members to establish the Oriental Library Revival Committee. Zhang Jusheng was elected as chairman, and Cai and Wang were elected as standing committee members. Pan Guanghui was appointed as secretary, responsible for carrying out all tasks.

International Support International academic and cultural circles are enthusiastic about planning the revival of the Oriental Library. Sponsorship committees will soon be organized in France, the United Kingdom, Germany and the United States. Zhang Xuelou will organize the British Sponsorship Committee, Oudemans will organize the German Sponsorship Committee, Li Rong will organize the French Sponsorship Committee, and Geller will organize the American Sponsorship Committee. Sponsorship committees will also be established in Nanjing, Hangzhou, Beiping, Guangzhou, Jinan, Hankou, and Changsha, with Luo Jialun, Guo Renyuan, Yuan Tongli, Quan Xiangfan, He Siyuan, Yang Duanliu, and Cao Dianqiu responsible for managing them respectively. They will be fully organized and established within a few days.

Collecting Books The most important task in the revival of the Oriental Library is the collection of books. Wang Yunwu told reporters yesterday that tens of thousands of volumes have been collected successively, including Commercial Press publications and private donations. After the establishment of domestic and international sponsorship committees, they will carry out their activities separately, and good results are expected. Recently, the German side has collected over 2,000 volumes of great works of French literature and chemical and pharmaceutical yearbooks as voluntary donations. These books will be shipped to Shanghai in the middle of next month. At the same time, in France, after Mr. Li Rong contacted the Minister of Education, the French government expressed sympathy and will also donate and ship a large number of valuable books to Shanghai recently. Private individuals in China are also very enthusiastic about donating. The method of collecting books is divided into two types: donation and loan. The Revival Committee will be responsible for the transportation costs of books donated or borrowed from various places.

Building a New Library All the books collected so far will be stored temporarily in a book storage room in Shanghai, which is currently located on the fourth floor of the Commercial Press Distribution Office. A plan to rebuild the Oriental Library is underway, with a budget of approximately 300,000 to 400,000 yuan, which will be grander than the previous building. It has been decided to allocate one-third of the Commercial Press's annual public welfare funds as the foundation. Over 45,000 yuan has been obtained for the previous year. Mr. Zhang Jusheng has personally donated 10,000 yuan. It is expected that the new library will be built in five years. The new location will be selected in the Jing'an Temple area of the city to facilitate public reading. Before the new library is built, all books will be temporarily rented in suitable locations and opened to the public to meet their needs.

Wang Yunwu's Final Words Wang Yunwu told the Shenshi News Agency reporter that when the Oriental Library was destroyed, his colleagues and others immediately made the decision to revive it. Due to the brutality of the Japanese, the international community is willing to provide active assistance. At that time, after the catastrophe, the Commercial Press itself still needed to be urgently restored, so he had no time to take care of it. Now that the Commercial Press's revival work is somewhat grounded, the revival of the Oriental Library is his most urgent task. He believes that one must first help oneself before seeking help from others. Considering the magnitude of the responsibility and in order to establish a comprehensive reference organization for the domestic academic community, he aims to expedite its realization and create a new dawn for the Chinese cultural cause.

Education Community's Rent Reduction Movement 180

Decides to Form a Committee to Respond to the Citywide Rent Reduction Association.

The Shanghai education community held a discussion meeting for principals at the Aiqun Girls' School on Daji Road yesterday afternoon at 2 PM to discuss the issue of reducing rent. More than 60 representatives from various schools attended. Ma Jiazhen presided over the meeting, and Zhang Lichun recorded the minutes. It was resolved to organize a rent reduction committee and to determine key issues such as rent reduction standards and the start date of the rent reduction. The details are as follows:

Attending Representatives Yesterday's attendees included Huang Zaoxiong from the Municipal Education Association, Xu Zeyu from Fudan Middle School, Ren Yingqian from Junyi Middle School, Wu Zhuanqian from Shanghai Girls' Middle School, Huang Sen from Zhengfeng Middle School, Ma Jiazhen from Huadong Girls' Middle School, Huang Zhengyi from Aiqun Girls' Middle School, Jin Yuezhang from Peiming Girls' Middle School, Fu Boliang from Xinhuan Vocational Middle School and Dunren Elementary School, Wang Guang from Songxue Elementary School, and representatives from over sixty public and private primary and secondary schools.

Resolutions After performing the usual rituals, the chairman gave a report, followed by discussion: (1) The number of rent reductions should be based on the discounts proposed by the Citywide Rent Reduction Association. The resolution was passed. (2) A committee should be organized by this association. The resolution was passed. Nine schools, including Junyi Middle School, Fudan Middle School, Shanghai Private Middle School, Hubei Middle School, Zhengfeng Middle School, Peiming Girls' Middle School, Songxue Elementary School, and Huadong Girls' Middle School, were elected to form the committee. (3) The rent reduction period should begin in February of the 23rd year of the Republic of China. The resolution was passed. (4) Legal advisors should be hired by this association. The committee members will provide written recommendations. (5) This association should participate in the Citywide Rent Reduction Movement Committee and act in unison. The resolution was passed. (6) The association's address should be the Municipal Education Association. The resolution was passed. (7) Schools that have not registered should be requested to continue registering separately. The resolution was passed.

News from Various Schools 185

Wusong Merchant Marine College: The Wusong Merchant Marine College, directly under the Ministry of Transportation, was destroyed during the Shanghai War two years ago and held classes in rented buildings in Shanghai. Last year, the original school was repaired and moved back. Since then, it has made every effort to reorganize. Not only has it restored its original state, but it has also expanded its facilities. Recently, a large open-air swimming pool has been constructed, and the Shanghai Dredging Bureau has been contracted to begin work. In addition, the drilling of an artesian well has also been put out to tender and submitted to the ministry. Furthermore, due to the inadequacy of the attached high school dormitory, it is planned to build ten new buildings. Drawings and designs have already been completed. It is also reported that the school's books and equipment suffered severe losses during the Shanghai War, and efforts have been made in recent years to replenish them. A large order has been placed with a major bookstore in Shanghai, with a total value of approximately five thousand yuan. The school currently has eight classes in both navigation and marine engineering (with four classes assigned to practice on ships in the Jianghai area and at the Jiangnan Shipyard), as well as one attached high school class. All regulations are more extensive and complete than before the Shanghai War. The second semester of the 22nd academic year began on the 1st of this month, and regular classes started today (the 5th). In addition, a memorial week was held at 10:00 AM this morning (Monday) in the school's auditorium. All faculty and students attended, and Principal Xu chaired the meeting, reporting on the progress of the previous semester and the various plans for this semester. The meeting concluded at 12:00 noon.

Shenmei Girls' High School: Shenmei Girls' High School on Maigen Road opened on the 1st. New and returning students have been enthusiastically registering at the school in recent days. At 9:00 AM yesterday, an opening ceremony was held in the school's auditorium, attended by over a hundred teachers and students. First, Principal Niu Changyao reported on the new plans for the next semester, followed by speeches from the director of discipline, Niu Xunyan, the registrar, Ren Dinghe, and teacher Zheng Fuqi. Regular classes at the school began today. There are still vacancies in various grades of the primary and secondary school departments. Students can enroll and take examinations at any time. Those with certification documents may be exempted from the entrance examination. Tuition fees may be reduced for those with financial difficulties.

Zhengyi Middle School: Zhengyi Middle School at 73 Moore Road opened on the 5th. In addition to the existing number of students, it is reported that fifty free places in junior high school have been specially offered to reduce the burden on students. Applications have been very enthusiastic in recent days. An examination was held on the 5th, and because the quota has not yet been filled, another examination will be held on the 10th.

World Billiards Master Smith to Show His Skills Tonight 188

Starting at 6:00 PM against Billiards King Li Gongying

Location: Lianhua General Association on Beijing Road

Willie Smith, the world-renowned professional billiards master, arrived in Shanghai yesterday morning aboard the President Jackson and is staying at the Huizhong Hotel. The Baohan Dun Club hosted a banquet to welcome him last night. Today, at 6:00 PM and 9:15 PM, he will hold exhibition matches with Shanghai amateur champion Li Gongying at the Lianhua General Association at 27 Beijing Road. The reporter visited him at his residence yesterday and had a long conversation. The details of his remarks are recorded below:

Addicted Since Childhood: I (Smith said himself) still remember that when I was ten and a half years old, I found billiards very fascinating. At the age of eleven, I was able to hold a cue. After following the elders, I gained some understanding of the skills and worked harder. I then associated with experts every day and learned all their secrets. Finally, I realized that my skills were comparable to those of world-class players, so I resolved to become a professional master, and today I have achieved my wish.

Two-Time Champion: In 1911, I transitioned from an amateur to a professional, and then traveled around the world. In 1920 and 1923, I won the British National Professional Championship twice in a row, setting a British record of 2743 points. This is my first time in China. I have long admired the prosperity of Shanghai, but since I have just unpacked my luggage, I have not yet toured the city, so it is difficult to express my feelings. Since leaving England, I have traveled through India, Malaysia, and Hong Kong, where I have competed. After completing my performances in Shanghai, I plan to return home on the 20th, as billiards players from all over the world have invited me to perform again.

An Honor: When I was in England, I knew that there were many Chinese students studying there who were proficient in this sport. Even during my performances on this trip, the excellent skills of the Chinese people I met always impressed me. There are especially many good players in Hong Kong. I feel very honored to be competing with the masters among the Chinese in Shanghai this time.

Eight Performances: Willie Smith will give eight performances in Shanghai. The Shanghai Amateur Billiards Association has specially commissioned the Englishman Mr. Bernal to select representatives to participate in the performances. Four Chinese players have been selected: Li Gongying, Shen Lince, Liu Fuzong, and Xu Shizhang, as well as the Portuguese player Medina Campos, and the Englishman Botto. There will be two sessions per day, the first session starting at 6:00 PM and the second session starting at 9:15 PM. Reserved seat tickets are three yuan per session and five yuan for two sessions. Non-reserved seat tickets are two yuan per session and three yuan for two sessions. The performance schedule is as follows:

April 4th: 6:00 PM, Li Gongying; 9:15 PM, Li Gongying

April 5th: 6:00 PM, Shen Lince; 9:15 PM, Xu Shizhang

April 6th: 6:00 PM, Liu Fuzong; 9:15 PM, Campos

April 7th: 6:00 PM, Botto; 9:15 PM, Medina

Jiaotong University and Beining Railway 191

| Ended with a 0-0 Draw | (Tianjin News) |

The Shanghai Jiaotong University football team's winter vacation tour northwards. At the end of last month, they arrived in Pingjin (Beijing and Tianjin). Of the two matches against Fu Jen and Qinghua, they had one loss and one draw. On the 1st of this month, the whole team took a train at 2:00 PM and arrived in Tianjin at about 5:00 PM that evening, lodging at the Rotary Middle School. At 3:00 PM yesterday afternoon, a special match was arranged at the Beining field against the Beining football team, the first match in Tianjin. Mr. Hou Luoxun was invited as the referee.

Match Situation: Both armies had changes in their lineups yesterday. Jiaotong University's Shen Guanlan and Wen Liandong were feeling unwell, so Shao Jihua was replaced as center back, and Gong Yibin as forward. Beining's Sun Fulai was absent, and Sun Guilin was changed to forward, with Pike filling the original position. When the whistle sounded on time, the deputy director of Beining performed the kickoff ceremony, and the charge began. Jiaotong University's front army had excellent communication and repeatedly invaded the enemy camp. Beining's defense was tight. Wang Baoshu showed his skills, and Sun Sijing was a one-man barrier, repeatedly thwarting the enemy's attacks. Veteran Pike was also quite brave and good at fighting. The front army quickly launched joint attacks, but missed several opportunities. At the end of the first half, neither side had scored. After the break, they changed positions and faced each other. Both sides were eager to attack, and the battle became more intense. Jiaotong University's Zhou Guangzhong and Wan Xianghua made several attempts to break through, but goalkeeper Chen Erde easily chased them down with his agility. Beining then attacked the enemy. Jiang Lu was extremely active. Jiaotong University's Wang Changying's crazy spirit was as strong as ever. In this battle, he was indeed Jiang Lu's strong opponent. There were two dangerous situations in front of the goal, but goalkeeper Fan Jiaju handled them well. Beining's Liu Zhongyuan was weak and missed the opportunity. When the whole game ended, both sides maintained a 0-0 tie, and they ended the battle with cheers.

Banquet: At about 7:00 PM that evening, the Beining Sports Association specially held a banquet at the main station cafeteria for the entire Jiaotong University team, and invited Mr. Hou Luosun and the press, as well as members of the association, to accompany them. During the banquet, Mr. Ma Yimin, the chairman of the association, gave a welcome speech, saying that it was a rare opportunity to have all the heroes gathered together. Jiaotong University and Beining are essentially one family, and those present are also close neighbors. He hoped that they would not be polite and would enjoy the meal. Then, the representative of the Jiaotong University team stood up and gave a speech, briefly saying that the Chinese people are only interested in sports during their student years, and when they enter society, they are separated from sports. However, the Beining Sports Association is enthusiastically carrying out its activities in this situation. We believe that the development of sports is closely related to the strength of a country. We hope that Beining will promote its spirit and guide social sports. The dinner lasted until 8:30 PM, when everyone dispersed in joy. The team will rest today, and at 2:30 PM tomorrow afternoon, they will play their second match in Tianjin against the Chinese team at the Nankai Middle School field. Tickets are available in two types, 10 cents and 20 cents. The lineups of both sides yesterday are recorded as follows:

Free Talk

Parrot Island and Parrots 193

— Gu Ming

Some time ago, it was reported that a large fire broke out on Parrot Island in Hankou, burning down more than 500 thatched cottages. This news has nothing to do with those who live in Shanghai洋房 (Western-style houses), but it makes one think of some old stories. || It is said that Parrot Island gets its name not because of the grass (芳草萋萋), but because a famous scholar was killed there || Zhengping. Those who have read Romance of the Three Kingdoms must know that this gentleman once beat a drum and scolded Cao Mengde. That is not credible. However, Cao Cao hated him very much and wanted to kill him, but fearing that he would ruin his own reputation, he sent him to Liu Biao. Liu Biao also hated him very much, probably because he was too proud, and was afraid of incurring a bad name (So he sent Heng to Huang Zu, the Governor of Jiangxia, who was impetuous). Later, the (impetuous) one really acted like a fool and killed him. He was 26 years old when he died.

Why were they so polite? Probably because at that time, the government and the public cherished young people with literary talent. It is a pity that he was a (rather obey and stay away from danger, rather not disobey and lose his life) person, like a parrot. And he did not know that once he entered the cage, there would be (no day to open the cage).

Not only was Mi Heng like this, but many scholars throughout history have been like parrots. They also speak human language, learn to sing, and may even understand a little bit of (the art of scolding people), but (they don't leave birds), (green clothes and jade collars) are not always pleasing to people. The parrot in Dream of the Red Chamber is hated by the maids. Of course, it's just a bird. But some parrots may love freedom. There was such a story before ||

Someone kept a parrot. One day, he met a monk, and the parrot asked him how to get out of the cage. The monk said harshly, (If you ask about the day you get out of the cage, unless your feet are straight!) The parrot heard this and suddenly got angry and died. The owner was very sad and blamed the monk for meddling, so he took it out and buried it. When he opened the cage, it flew away.

Thinking of Wandering 194

— Liu Ming

Although it was a long time ago, it still makes me yearn when I think about it now.

Wearing my pattering wooden clogs, taking advantage of the fine rain, on a misty autumn morning, I boarded the southward bound ship on the Irrawaddy River and left Bhamo. Seeing the willows standing gracefully in the misty rain on both banks, gradually receding, blurring, and disappearing in the mist, the joy of traveling and wandering floated vividly and strongly in my heart. Even now, I still think that getting on that journey was the most unforgettable pleasure in my life.

Because before, in the spring, I had wanted to rely on this southern river to go to a more distant place, but I was forced by life to the point where it was difficult to even stay in Bhamo. Finally, I was forced back to the Neren Mountain in the north to spend the hard days of sweeping horse manure, and spent a full five months.

Thinking about it now, if there had been no such experience, then the interest in gazing at the exotic rain scene from the deck of the ship would not have been so strong or so heavy. Therefore, I can say that impoverished wandering is more interesting and particularly nostalgic than affluent travel. But this requires a person with a long-term depressed mood to appreciate this meaning - if he has not actually wandered.

Chekhov, who is good at writing about the depression of intellectuals, I think, his mood must have been extremely depressed, right? Bunin, who won the Nobel Prize last year, once described that before he died, Chekhov often said loudly in his sleep (become a wanderer, a pilgrim, go to those holy places, live in temples, forests, lakesides; on summer evenings, sit on a bench in front of a Muslim church···). What a longing for wandering!

I myself traveled from Sichuan to Myanmar entirely on bare feet, walking those difficult Yunnan mountain roads, and in Kunming and Yangon, I had the misery of being evicted from the store for failing to pay the rent. In reason, whether in terms of mood or body, I should be tired of wandering. But now, when I mention wandering, I still yearn for it, and feel that it is the most enchanting thing in life. Why? I don't know. Perhaps this is because the heavy depression is still deeply pressing on my heart? However, when I think about the time when I should give up this kind of personal pleasure, the beautiful lakes and mountains in the distance, and the unknown grasslands, I have no choice but to let them lie idle at the end of the world.

Momentous Occasion 195

— Wei Mengke

Snow was flying, and the weather was very cold.

Although this auditorium was small, it was created by combining a classroom, and it still managed to fit three hundred desks. The doodles of female students' faces and legs, carelessly drawn on the desks with pencils, were, exceptionally, washed off by the school janitor with several buckets of water. The left corner of each desk also had a numbered sticker, neatly affixed. Usually, there were no stoves in the classrooms, but today there were not only stoves but as many as three. Once the windows were closed, the heat became overwhelming; even after taking off one's coat, one still felt bloated. If it weren't for the snow flying outside, we might have suspected that spring had arrived. The school authorities had gone to such lengths to prepare the examination hall; even if one couldn't call it magnificent, in our hearts, we all thought it was more than adequate. What's more, what flags and portraits had been newly added to the whitewashed wall behind the podium?

Before the bell rang, the students were already rushing in, vying to be first. In Shanghai's universities, there were few students as enthusiastic about exams as these. We were remarkably relaxed and calm, huddled tightly around the three stoves: chatting, laughing, bickering, even fighting. In short, as far as exams were concerned, we were supremely confident.

Yes, we were indeed confident about the exams. When the bell rang, we went to our assigned seats (according to our numbers), opened our inkstones, and dipped our brushes. Each of us took out a draft we had prepared a week earlier. We continued to chat and laugh, calmly waiting for the mimeographed questions and answer sheets to be distributed so we could begin our work.

The proctor—the Dean of Academic Affairs, Mr. Liu, with his beard—specially donned a cyan silk mandarin jacket, carried a stack of exam papers, stroked his walrus mustache, and walked in heavily. He stood silently by the door for two or three minutes, scrutinizing the various faces, before pacing over and carefully distributing the questions and answer sheets according to the seat numbers. He put on a stern face and warned: (Work carefully; the papers are not allowed to be swapped.)

The exam then began, and the atmosphere became tense. Mr. Liu paced heavily back and forth in silence. When he spotted laughter on one side, he rushed over, glared, and issued a warning: (Um...). Suddenly, several faces appeared pressed against the glass windows of the examination hall, emitting suppressed laughter. This greatly angered Mr. Liu, who quickly shouted: (Hey! What are you looking at?) But this was not only ineffective; the number of faces gradually increased, and the laughter became even louder. Although Mr. Liu was very solemn, he was ultimately helpless against these faces and could only randomly ask: (What's your name?) (Which department are you in?)

It was no wonder Mr. Liu was angry. The current term exam had become a most momentous occasion; how could he allow students from other departments to disrupt it! In the past, he would have let them make as much noise as they wanted, but now the school had just been registered; if the Ministry found out, that would be terrible. We all sympathized with Mr. Liu. In the tense atmosphere, we could even cheer up and quickly finish the exam so we could return to the stoves to chat. Now that they were making such a racket, our thoughts were distracted. If our essays hadn't been prepared so short, we probably wouldn't even be able to finish copying them! The exam ended in less than half an hour. Mr. Liu carefully collected the papers according to the numbers, stroked his walrus mustache, and heavily paced out the door. We huddled around the three stoves again, and the students who had been idle outside, with their frozen, rosy faces, squeezed in.

Snow was flying, and the weather was very cold.

Liang Rengong in Hunan (3) 196

— Yu Shixia

Liang Rengong's writing style also had a great impact in Hunan. In those days, who didn't enjoy reading the articles in the *Shiwu Bao* (Current Affairs)? Even the old-fashioned scholars had no objections. But because Liang Rengong went to Hunan to lecture, and new Hunan figures published *Xiangxue Bao* (Hunan Studies) and *Xiang Bao* (Hunan News), this incurred the great resentment of the old Hunan scholars. Therefore, in his letter to Ye Dehui, Pi Xirui said:

"Literary men despise each other; this has been the case since ancient times. The people of Hunan lack regional solidarity and enjoy attacking each other. They praise the *Shiwu Bao* but denigrate the *Xiangxue Bao*; the criticisms of *Xiang Bao* are even more severe. The ingrained habits of the Hunan people are not surprising."

It turned out that Mr. Ye was a leader of the old faction who attacked the new faction. It wasn't enough for him to attack the ideas of the Kang-Liang faction; he also wanted to attack their writing style. In his letter to Mr. Pi, he said: "The writing style of the times has long been criticized by the learned. The learned are often unable to write in that style; those with high talent and broad learning are trapped in their studies, while those who speculate and imitate achieve success. But if we replace the style with policy essays, the drawbacks would be the same. Don't you see today's exam papers, filled with nothing but words like 'starting point,' 'pressure,' and 'thermal power'? It's all empty talk; why invite such ridicule!"

He attacked the policy essays in the new style for merely using new terms and being just as empty as the eight-legged essay. He also said in a letter to a friend: "What is most ridiculous is that they exhaust their pens and tongues, calling themselves 'Zhi Na' (China); they always say 'starting point' as the first basis. They don't consider that 'Zhi Na' is the Buddhist term for Tang China, and 'starting point' is the interpreter's term for calculation. In terms of language, it is translated into words; in terms of writing, it is spelled out into characters. It is neither writing nor substance, neither Chinese nor Western. Is this not Dong Shi imitating Xi Shi, inviting the laughter of the neighboring girls?"

This was also an attack on articles using new terminology. Moreover, the Hunan Provincial Academy Covenant, in the article "Distinguishing Writing Styles," said:

"The court believes that the accumulated abuses of the eight-legged essay are too deep, so it has changed the exam to policy essays. However, the policy essays in the examination hall do not involve scholarship; those who can write well control them, and their abuses are probably even worse than those of the eight-legged essay. Looking at the works published in the *Xiang Bao*, such as 'thermal power,' 'expansion power,' 'love power,' 'absorption power,' 'attraction power,' 'pressure,' 'Zhi Na,' 'Zhendan,' 'starting point,' 'forming lines,' 'blood wheel,' 'brain,' 'soul,' 'ether,' 'yellow race,' 'white race,' '400 million people,' etc., they come as soon as the pen moves. Some people like to use all kinds of obscure and strange words, and one becomes breathless before finishing a single chapter." It can be seen that more than thirty years ago, the use of new terms in articles by the new faction was the most hated thing by the old faction scholars. At that time, the popularity of this new writing style in Hunan could be said to have been brought by Liang Rengong. It was no wonder that a group of old-faction scholars in Hunan, who had started with the eight-legged essay, were both jealous and indignant that the Examination Commissioner Xu actually used this style of writing to select scholars.

Liang Rengong once said that his own writing (always carried emotion in the pen), which was true. He was a political commentator, and the emotion in his pen was one of the factors that allowed his political commentary to sweep the world. This kind of writing, suitable for agitation, was brought to Hunan. A tribute student learned it very well. This person was called Fan Chui, from Shaoyang. He published some articles in the *Xiang Bao*. The most attacked article by the old faction was titled "Sincerity," which said:

"The people have been foolish for too long, and they have not seen the light of day for too long. Those above use this to fool them, and those below passively accept it. For two thousand years, it has penetrated their muscles and soaked into their marrow, shackling their dreams and imprisoning their souls, reveling in the sea of suffering and hell, galloping in the land of drunken life and nightmare death, binding them, trampling on them, like cattle and horses, like moss."

This was a scathing denunciation of the policy of fooling the people for more than two thousand years, and the thought was rather unstable. It also said: "Now it is appropriate that from the officials to the commoners, all should be like this, gathered together in one room, confined and closed, so that they do not see the sun and the moon, and are not covered by the earth." How thorough was this way of dealing with corrupt officials! His arguments were even more radical. He also said: "Therefore, I wish that His Majesty would wield a five-inch pipe, half a pool of ink, without asking anyone, without consulting the masses, and issue an edict that must be carried out. It should say, 'Now that things have come to this, danger is imminent, although there is a present, it is useless. Rather than dissecting and dismembering, giving every inch to others, where can we moor our carriage, and there is no way to reach the sky. It is better to take advantage of the fact that it is not yet rotten and make it public to the world. Let me be finished!'"

His argument was truly bold. No wonder the old faction rebuked him, saying: "The emperor's edict, how dare subjects presume to imitate it, let alone utter such rebellious words! The national laws are in place; cutting him into pieces, inch by inch, is not enough to cover his guilt." He also said in the article:

"Wash away the old habits, follow justice, then all the complicated rituals, the despicable nobility, the evil examples and inferior models of civil and military fame, the erroneous clauses and chaotic chapters of selection files, major political laws, universal constitutions and equal laws, schools for the four peoples, customs and folk customs, all must be changed from the past, and searched without leaving anything behind, only the West is the model, using Confucius's era for dating."

How could such a thorough transformation and reform be achieved at that time? But he could not help but advocate it. He was the extreme new faction in Hunan. He was more thorough than Liang Rengong's ideas, and his arguments were more radical than Liang Rengong's. He fully demonstrated the extreme characteristics of the Hunan people. However, he was the person most deeply influenced by Liang Rengong.

It's ridiculous to say. Around the year of the Wuxu Reform (1898), Liang Rengong was too new; around the year of the Xinhai Revolution (1911), Liang Rengong was old again; around the time of the May Fourth Movement (1919), Liang Rengong (running after the younger generation) couldn't catch up. This great era was a bit of a trickster. Although the times are always moving forward, if people don't stand before the times, they fall behind the times. Is there anything surprising about that?

The Wet Nurse (4) 197

— Xu Zhuanpeng

(He suddenly started to cry.) She lowered her head in shame.

(The child is crying, and still I don't hear you making a sound. Are you asleep?)

(No, Madam, I am awake.) (Why don't you hum him to sleep? This child has a temper; if you hum for a while, he will stop crying.) The Madam said. After thinking for a moment, she asked: (Can you hum a little tune?)

(I can't.) (Like this, (Hum, hum, little darling, go to sleep, hum, hum...) can't you do that? Truly a country person; when the child cries, you don't even make a sound...)

After that, on quiet evenings, when the child was crying, one could hear the wet nurse humming in her coarse voice: (Hum, hum, little darling,

go to sleep, hum, hum...)

(5) The wet nurse had been in her home for one month, lacking only four days, precisely one hundred days after the child was born into this world. They were preparing to host a banquet for the child. Two days before, the Madam said to the wet nurse: (The day after tomorrow is the child's hundredth day; we're planning to have a feast and invite many relatives and friends to shave the child's head!) The clear-faced, thin child had only been by the wet nurse's side for more than twenty days, and having drunk her milk, he was as plump as a vegetable in a garden after fine rain. The child was very lively and lovable, with dark eyes and a high, carp-backed nose. That day, the child had his head shaved and wore a new blue checkered outfit that harmonized with the colors of early summer. A silver neck chain hung with a string of silver bells, and with the slightest movement, it would ring (jingle).

The aunts, the Madam's younger sister, the Madam's old classmates living in the city, and some female guests had all arrived. Each of them, upon arriving and without sitting down, asked with great concern: (Where is the young master?) The wet nurse hid in the room with the child, as if she was afraid of seeing the guests. Today, the child was dressed up, and the wet nurse had also dressed up, with powder on her face and the female cook having trimmed her face. She wore the white bamboo cloth short shirt and pants. She was called by the Madam from the room into the living room filled with guests, holding the child for the guests to see. They took turns praising the child: (The child is so lovable, with a high nose like his father.) Someone would then chime in: (And a pair of dark eyes just like his mother!)

Silver Coin Position Excess, Foreign Currency Break Opened for White Borrowing 200

Yesterday's foreign currency discount market price surprisingly saw cash concentration. The excess cash position, combined with the overall closing relationship, led to a scarcity of supply, resulting in an egregious oversupply. Both the morning and afternoon markets opened for white borrowing, with very little trading. The situation was extremely loose, and the headliner was also white-washed without adding water. Banks also had many positions and no way to place them. The amount of cash positions in the financial sector was rarely seen in previous years. The bill discount transaction only had 2.78 million in the morning transfer and more than 500,000 in new transactions. The afternoon had 300,000 to 400,000 transactions, and the small general meeting had more than 500,000 transactions. The total cash notes retrieved and issued were only 1.3 to 1.4 million. Chinese banks received more than 4.7 million in silver loan notes, more than 4.5 million in settlement loans, more than 2.9 million in special loans, various freight exchange mortgage loans, tax and miscellaneous loans of more than 5.6 million, and more than 500,000 withdrawn from the warehouse. Japanese banks received more than 500,000 in settlement loans and more than 2.3 million in foreign currency, silver deposited in the warehouse was 400,000 and 600,000 in foreign currency. The money shops received more than 45 million in foreign currency loans and more than 940,000 in foreign currency transfer loans, customer exchange loans were more than 40,000, and the cash received was 300,000 to 400,000. The total number of exchanges at the local clearing house on the 5th was 9,732,861 yuan, 6 jiao and 3 fen, including 4,897,547 yuan and 7 fen in silver yuan and 4,835,314 yuan, 5 jiao and 6 fen in foreign currency transfer.

Securities and Bond Market: Chaotic Fluctuations with Little Movement 202

｜Pre-Closing Situation Comparatively Firm｜

｜Stock Exchange Closed for Nine Days Starting from the 10th｜

Yesterday, at the Chinese Merchants Securities Exchange, the market initially remained chaotic, but showed signs of strengthening. The market slightly improved at closing, and the trend is unlikely to reverse in the short term. However, there are unlikely to be major fluctuations before the Lunar New Year. Short sellers, finding no way out, are slightly covering their positions, but most are patiently waiting for opportunities, remaining in a wait-and-see state. Sharp rises in market prices will inevitably be followed by sudden drops. A slow, gradual increase is not in the interest of short sellers, but only sudden rises and drops can shake the defenses of both sides. A long period of brewing will lead to significant changes. Yesterday’s trading appeared chaotic and uncertain on the surface, with very slight fluctuations. After the afternoon closing, the upward trend was relatively firm. In the morning sessions and at the opening of the afternoon session, prices saw mixed ups and downs, but each session had more gains than losses, by about five cents to twelve cents. Notably, the No. 75 short positions were covered, and No. 64 saw considerable buying interest. Other transactions were not very active, with retail investors dominating trading, and arbitrage transactions were limited. As a result, market prices improved slightly by five cents to forty-five cents. Among these, the forward contracts for One Nine Dragon and One Nine Good Twenty fluctuated slightly, decreasing by five cents to one and a half cents. However, the 22nd Year Customs Bonds suddenly fell by more than one dollar and twenty cents. Regarding this type of treasury bond trading, the reporter believes it has not yet entered the right track. The total turnover was 11,393,000 yuan, including 3,000 yuan in spot transactions. Futures included 3,890,000 yuan in unified salt tax, 1,700,500 yuan in disarmament bonds, 550,000 yuan in 19 Customs Bonds, 2,120,000 yuan in 20/20 bonds, 1,790,000 yuan in gold short contracts, 740,000 yuan in 96 contracts, and the remainder ranged from 120,000 yuan to over 200,000 yuan. The market announced that it would be closed for seven days from February 10th to 17th, with a regular Sunday holiday on the 18th. Normal business would resume on the 19th.

New York Stock Market Active and Trending Higher 203

According to a report from New Asia Trading Company, on the 3rd, the New York stock market rose several cents to two dollars. Trading was extremely active, driven by excellent reports from the automotive and steel industries. The New York City bank clearinghouse saw a sharp increase in exchange amounts, and a portion of cotton sales exceeded 60% of production. Bonds were also active and slightly higher. Half-day trading volume reached 2,081,170 shares. Wheat prices rose by a little over one cent due to short covering. Spot prices were strong, and the market has the potential for a sharp rise. Cotton spot prices remained tight, and the large volume of outstanding orders from yarn factories strengthened the market. Reductions in cotton acreage and continued commercial progress are key factors determining market prices in the long term. Brokers generally have bullish views, and the market is firm.
